et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and one of the cleavings also as two five all the middle part in swallowing until neif, and the others two at the costles above the papers, and keep back from incising the arteries that are above the papers;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and remove your hand from the extension of the two mandibles, and be each wound the quantity of three halves at the four joints;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have laid out a piece of sponge and mowed the drapels there for to wipe away the blood, then pour the water from two parts where it is this shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incisions that are to be made on the temple until the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and peel all the skin that is between the two cleavings up to all the medicine that is on the bone, then do the same thing from the middle incison until the other second, and then remove far this sponge.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put in the first cut the instrument that is called "culteller", and it is very well sharpened on one side, and the other is smooth, not sharpened, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	and set the knife-edge cutting toward the cart at the back, and the edge is smooth towards the bone, and put it in as far as it comes to the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the hairs that descend from the head as long as the incision is continuous until it opens at the curb, and then make another halfway cut until the other end.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then remove the hair evenly, and press down on the spot where the hair has been removed;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	and then put a piece of cotton tent in each cut, and put there drapings soaked in wine and oil and honey, and watch so that the abscesses do not come out;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and for three days leave it alone, and I bring a great quantity of aquatic tar, then the treatment with basilic oil mixed with rose oil, and other treatments to treat wounds, as long as he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Let the hairs remain.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When any patient comes with a catarrh that has been habitual, and you see the hairs turning gray and fine, and weakening vision, and burned papers;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair is cut, and where it hurts most, the patient sneezes.
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	So that we may know that these matters and this discharge do not come from many veins, but only from one, this is the cure that I give.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you command the patient to raise his forehead, then make a large incision at the forehead, and another one wide apart.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin from the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision just to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and remove your hand from the nerves of the temples that move with chewing;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, so suck up all the blood with a sponge, and then tie it between the two lips of the incision with cotton and linen;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then lay there drapings moistened in wine and oil, and keep the abscess warm;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	and when it is uncovered, if you rub the bone so that the blood begins to flow, then treat with drying things, which cause chapping.
En teil maniere:	In one way:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of wheat flour, and three parts of colophony, and make an ointment out of it;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and apply it to the wounds to stop the disease from spreading.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the support of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All who have an ear are one of the four:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grain, or beast, or stone of a certain size, or some other thing like it.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, such as wheat, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing thing, such as water and other similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it rings in the ear due to a stone or some other object that does not fit into the ear, and does not stay in place, put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, then distil no oil of violets or sesame oil, but instead introduce an extract;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and let it cool down, and stop up the nostrils with cloth or wool when the cooling down is done, and place it near the ear;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and raise the ear up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times this remedy comes out strongly.
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come out strongly, then administer to her extraction with subtle needles, for the form is:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	if it comes out well with the needles, it is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, then extract with a subtle tiny hook;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if not by the hook, then make a knife of iron and a bottle with a sharp edge at the top or the opening of the ear, and stop up what is inside with soft wax so that the liquid cannot enter with the knife;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then firmly press it down, for many times this comes out strongly as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come out in any way, then take some glue and press the ears, and put in some instrument that is right for the needle to go through, and put a little cotton inside;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the meat onto the stone or something, and keep it firm.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if she doesn't get well from all of the things we've said, then you must quickly split the ear so that it cracks and convulses.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	And the way to handle the split so that you make the first rescue of the headache, and extract the blood according to its virtue, then sit the headache between your hands and turn it upside down, and cut a small split in the root of the ear at the fat or where it depends;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the split be as if it were a moon, until you press it against the stone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it carefully into your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it's a grain that has grown large, then administer an extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if he cannot come out, then bring the spatula gently and carefully according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and provide an incision for that seed.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do so when you think that the grain is moist because of the moisture in the ear, until you have made many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then remove it with small pincers and a scalpel, as we said, so that the extractions are orderly.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	Therefore, when a person has a cold in their ear, they should first use a strong expectorant, and widely wrap the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him go to bed with that ear up where the cold is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	if it bleeds, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	if not, then take many pearls according to the length of your finger towards and lightly, and heat them a little on the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put the patient a piece of his ear, and slice on one side of his pieces from another part, and fix with another piece on the piece that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not stop to make a piece of stone after a piece until the water comes out all the way, and so does it all the way;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see, if burn I a joint, and pour one of the heads in the ear, and the other head take fire until the more strong joint is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	and then repair another part of the others as much water as comes out, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the animal, if it is a small horn, as a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the dislocation;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is a large horn so that one can feel it, then do the extraction with tweezers;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the lighter thing to open which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms embedded in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the dislocation and where we have spoken of the treatments for distillation, and the treatment does not benefit, then you should look at the ear towards the sun:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If there is no opening towards the outside, if the thread is very thin, and if it does not open, take hold of the string where it is curved.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	It is narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And cut the thinnest part of the ear according to the quantity of pain in the patient, and then suck off the form with all the string;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this often until all the blood comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, then stop it with cotton inside as I have said in the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not flow strongly as we have said, administer distillations that the old ones have tried in the extraction of worms, and you will find them or administrator of the distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distill your oils and medicines in the ear with all this instrument, of which form it is as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And let silver or gold be melted down into small pits, and above them pour to distill.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and for pressing within the distillation to the instrument of silver well made for this, and take you a razor and wrap it around the tip forward cotton;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then pour in your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the cane, and the cane be in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then bottle into the razor all cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or drawn from the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and let the patient breathe it in, and let the distillation be heated as one would distil it in the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and keep it from being too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the support of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who does not have small pits in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and these things also happen to people by a wound in the ear, or a nail inside the ear, and these wounds never completely heal if one cannot see them.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and never does one get a pimple on the nose, and see well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	that comes completely, if one cannot see it, is of great healing in many cases, and in this case you should put the ear of the patient in the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the operation clearly, if the surgery is done completely with this liquid that gives form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	and be agile and cut before and behind everything, so that it doesn't tear the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the operation is a nail or a piece of bone in the ear, if you hold it with delicate pincers and cut it lightly, until the whole nail is removed;
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the ear is fully formed, then take a sharp and light razor and heat it slightly over fire, and then put the ear ring in.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the swelling that the patient feels pain when he hears it, pierce lightly and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then put a cotton swab in the ear according to its width, and oil it with Egyptian oil.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do not put anything inside for a day until the wound is healed, or you take a cotton swab and soak it in rosewater, and powder it with vinegar powder;
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see the ear draining, if it is possible that you take out the cotton swab and insert another wet cotton swab made of rosewater oil and wax, until the drain is dried up;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is well.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the pain comes on, dip a sponge and drape in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other remedies that relieve the pain of the headache which are or treating distillations.
de la char des papieres	with paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	Take a string from the hair when it is moist and dry, if it is possible that you spread them with pliers and tweezers, and cut them with a spatum of their roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Then place over the vitriol fire.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if not peeled, then place the fire cautery, after the cauldron-like fire cautery, and let it cool after cutting.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and often return, such that nothing remains rooted in its place;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And when they are burned by fire, if the roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the root
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Often come in papers the hairs a thing that seem gressly in its form and in its dureness, and for this is this disease called "grene", and is an assembly of moisture thick on top of the paper above and below;
li ovraiges est telz:	The over-workings are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	take ward that the grene moves from one side to the other, and this is a light thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Do the scraping of each part lightly, then take it in pinches, and finally bind it up.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cover it up without piercing a bit of paper, do not cause any harm to the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the fracture is great, and put together with a stitch, and heal as long as it is well;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not make any effort, for soon it will heal and cause pain again.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the swelling is descending from the ear towards the upper part, turn over the paper and place the swelling on some pins, and cover and press from both sides;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is moved by the incision, that does not cause any harm;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the swelling has been covered, let there be salt water applied, and heal the part where it hurts as long as the patient is well.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat from the hair
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Enchaine is fat that is caught in webs of paper above, and this happens more often to children than to others, and hurts their eyes, and they come out with the catarrh in the mornings, and cannot bear to look at the light of the sun because of their tears.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and so they lay on their faces together, and sleep, and are in their skins wet from the coldness of the water which is opened in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the neck to your ears and feel the pulse run between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the way of this remedy is that the patient put his head on the ground;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then he takes a blanket of linen, and prepares a tent in the form of a circle according to the quantity of the exiniach of each part, and puts it on him;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your hands from both sides so that the exiniach is gathered together in the middle of the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	and then pour into the middle of the moisture the spatemile cutting a slant with its broad edge, and it should not be any larger than the wound that is made at the opening of the vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and then make the skin smooth in perfection until you come to the exiniach;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and multiple disorders come from the wound, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	So take out all one piece of drying cloth between your two hands and turn your hand from right to left as it dries.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and keep you from stretching the wound, that you do not come to all the splint until it is oil, that you do not bleach it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the extraction does not cause difficulty in the wound, then slightly open the wound lightly until it is visible;
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then extract it as we have said, then wet the drapels with water and put them on their place, and extract the splints.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind leaven and put it on top so that the moisture that is delayed is corrupted.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal it until it is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the apothema hot, if the healer of wounds assuages it until it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When the hairs come out by themselves and are worn out, if they damage the eyes, and cause ways of diseases as usual tears and softening of the hairs and albaugine, so that it is a cause of the destruction of the eyes;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and he has four ways to treat it:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by fire cautery, or by medicine as much as he is before, or by the paste of cauterization, and it is made or by incising and sewing or by cutting, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your right hand, then bring the paper of oil to your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is turned over, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, pour a little needle on all the thread above;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and if that is too small at the edge of the paper where the hairs grow out from these hairs, and thread all the way up to the paper, and turn it back to the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make the part of the paper smooth, smoothing out the hairs, all the way up to the skin with a little blade, from the large wound down to the small one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Then draw out the thread, and place a little tent of cotton and drape on the paper, then sign on the paper a figure of an arm, like the husk of mirth, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity which you see raise the paper which is devised for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if the place where it is necessary that it is made a little quantity of the paper according to what the paper is softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then mark all the spine on the two lines that you have signed, and begin with great tears until small;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let it be a fracture near the hairs by the thickness of a root, then pour the vinegar in one of the two angles from which it comes, and then peel it all off;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then assemble the two lips to a stitch of a needle with all the fine thread, and wipe off the blood, and make air the excess of the threads on the two sicles about anything sticky, if you see to do so;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, if you are not worried about it, then leave the sewing and the thread until three days or four.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then treat the wound without sewing with dry and constricting things, because the paper softens at the touch of the wound and the bandage, but the sewing is dried (as the old say), and this is done without fear;
et si a une autre maniere:	and if there is another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you sign the paper with a shape that is like the fern frond, as we have told, at three times according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off those who are at the top with small forces evenly according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you do not have the ability to hold the pliers, and the thing is not even, take an needle with a thread, and wrap it around the shape;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and bottle another fine thread, and a long one, and a small one, and join them together evenly between your two hands;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then hold your hand evenly, and hold all the skin over it where you have sewn it, as we have told you, and join the two lips of the wound with a stitch, and treat it until it is healed.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, if you apply cerotin and similar ointments that soothe it;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and no time has passed that the hair of the paper has been turned:**
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	then you must use what we have said about the incision:**
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitch on one side and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of dog bites is done according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and you should turn the paper and put it in according to what I have said, and then make two holes with a sharp instrument, and two thin strings as long as the paper and the width of the spatumile is:**
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut off both ends where you hold the threads.
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then bring together the two slowly above that which rises from the paper of the oil, and draw out the two strands from the two parts formed;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it like this for a few days, and the skin that has been drawn out will harden and shrivel and rot, until it is gone on its own.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it takes too long, if the cut is strong, then treat it until it is healthy;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound has healed, and if the paper has been raised, and the hair will no longer grow;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	This is the form of the two strands that you shall make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the ovraige is such that you squeeze a small needle, and I thread a fine and thin silk thread;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	and then join the heads together and arrange them carefully, so that the length of the thread is a palm's length.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	and then order in the chase another thread of silk briefly, and tie the heads with the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then put the patient's head on your shoulder;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and then take the sun' s help so that the work is gentle and subtle, then stick the needle into all the hair at the base, and pierce it into the paper carefully while you hold it on top of the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then remove the hair all the way up to the head, and stick the same hair into the head, if there is one or two or three or more;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then remove your hand until the hairs come out all the way up to the head, mixed in with the natural hair, on the paper;
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if it is chased away, treat it and the hairs will not come out with it, so you will take the chase to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes out of the hole above and you see it by the sight of oil;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	And if you chase it and the thread, and close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and the scar comes out;
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are small, so accompany one long hair of nature, and be lifted with it or leave it, until it is lengthened and then let it down.
de la porriture de l’oil	And if he is chased, he is treated; and the hairs do not come with him, if you will spin the tow from the sheep's wool at a distance, so that it comes from the head of the sheep, and then you will see it through the sight of the eye; then if you will spin the tow and the yarn, and harden the oil and leave it hardened for II days or III, so that the hair grows in its place and the curl rises up; and if the hairs are small, then accompany a long hair with natural curly hair, and be carried with that which you leave, so that it is lengthen and then let it lie.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the porridge comes in oil, there are two ways:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and one unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And happens suddenly by wound, or by cut, or by cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way of healing it in itself is that you split that seam, and separate the lips of it, and put linen threads inside, and let them heal until they are well;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not necessary that you use in the cure of them things that dry and restrain.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but I have experienced things that soften, as fennel;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the rose of water or salt and flax seeds are cooked, and olive oil is melted in any of the oils, and it encloses a tent, and cure this with it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your cure is that you give yourself in defense so that it does not harden according to the form that it was before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and the remedies we have said are that we do not give ourselves in defense from this disease, so that it does not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	the oil comes from the lard
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	this disease that is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and burns and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way of this extract is that you should squeeze an needle, in that it has a double thread, and the thread to the cart, and make it pierce from the left side of the ear so much on the right, that the thread comes in two shoulders of the cart;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then place the cart above all the needle, and the cloth to the large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper comes back according to what it is that it should be, it is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, take the razor and put it in the split, and turn the paper, and make two splits where it is inside the paper;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the shoulders of the two splits be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and let one angle be so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter that has not "I griesche";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	and then cut off that bone, according to the quantity that its sides are open, from what encloses the paper, and then join together the two feared parts, and the cost of a sheep's yarn;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then the treatment for that which we have said regarding the soothing medicines, and bandages, until it is well.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a cut, or a stitch, or a cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain cut through the hairs of the paper, and according to what is above.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	and then join together between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and the work must be done according to the shape of the disease, for it is very different in form, and the master surgeon arranges everything within his power so that he can restore the shape to its natural state;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient's middle ones, according to what must be done with the tools and the art of many arrangements.
dou soudement de la papiere	And if the patient comes from a cut, or a stitch, or a cauterization, it is convenient that you make a plain cut out of the hair of the patient, and according to what is said above  ; then loosen between the II books of a tent, as I have said  ; and it is necessary to do the work according to the form of the disease, because it is very diverse in shape, and the master sagacers will apparill the tool according to all its power to bring back the figure to its natural shape  ; and the patient himself, according to what convenes of work and instruments in diverse dispositions.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this weld is made in such a way that the paper above is welded with the oil white, and cannot move or do its natural work, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor to weld the paper, and lift it up;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and they are spread out as pins, as much as you can take what is made on the thin blade of a pin, which is not too sharp and not too dull, so that the patient does not suffer from the too sharp blade of the pin, which bleeds the oil;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and be your incision, where you peel off that which is assembled, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and all that is gathered is healed, and never put in acidic salt, and raise it with fresh water and wine;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	Then place between the paper and the oil a piece of linen cloth, and place on the oil wet wool in abundance of smoke.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after three days use the collar and the things that bind together until it is well.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the finger is according to two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	It is nervous and resembles a hard matter of blood, and another that is not nervous but resembles frozen moisture, which when touched with iron and heated with pinches does not burn.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	And both these appearances begin to spread towards the great tear, and grow more and more until they blind all sight and all light and all movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the way of the incision is that the patient puts his head in the sun, then he opens the hair;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and hold the paper to your hand, then twist the nail around the little finger, and extend it upward;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	and take a needle, and I put a hair of horse, or of cow, or of bull, and thread it tightly;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and thread it through the nail, and pierce it with all the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it up, and peel off at all the nails' ends the rind of the nail which follows the tendon and the silk to the hair root until the top, then cut the remaining in the root of the nail so that by the incision does not come out the blood as is used;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and never stretch the nail to the one-sided cut, and on the thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	and then burn everything with a fire so that this is the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	and keep the spatem away from the raw flesh and don't tear it, and don't pierce the prune.
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision pour in oil a little rope of tar and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal what needs to be healed as much as possible so that it is healthy.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	and if the nail is not nervous, and you can't put in a needle, and this image of a nail with medicine is often healed.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and come like I have told you in the division, and if you see it covered, so work on the oil of the sick man, and take a little spatem according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And stretch out the finger carefully, and if you see that it is not shrinking at all and its growth is accelerated, then distil from your mouth in oil made of litargite and red dye and honey, and stop the oil until the next day.
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And then begin again with this same work on the other hand, as long as it is all boned.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes it in the oil, as if it were a hot abscess, then the milk, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healthy, then begin the operation again as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh of the arm hurts a lot in the oil, then hang it on a hook, and make a covering with a part of it, not all at once, so that tears do not come.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And then distil in the red oil which is made of litargite.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the horse that was born with a foal on its eye
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	Of some men there are none that do not make the red color, and they crush the prunes and hold them on the paper and turn them away from themselves, and it seems like a rose of bumblebee.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and if the patient puts his head in your lap, then he will operate on the hairs, and tie all those that suit him with appropriate knots for that, and support it firmly.
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then shave the first hair, and keep shaving until the end, and be careful not to spill the oil on the patient while operating.
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and be the incision of the spurium that we have said in the incision of the nail and with small movements so that one breaks the bone with force, as the form after this chapter shows.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is complete and all the hair has been removed, then pour on the oil of rose or you have distilled with red wine and similar medicines that are corrosive, and put a cotton ball on top with the help of honey, so that it is assured against an abscess heating.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if there is a delay and the sun rises on you, and you doubt about the abscess heating, then leave the oil and treat the abscess with soothing things that heat the abscess.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and return to your work as soon as you are well, and so make the skin tight with this treatment.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	However, it is necessary that you adjust the cure for each person according to their natural path.
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and of the route of accident, in work with iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that the limbs are suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the hairs
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	are red, and are covered over the oil, and endure its work and weaken the oil all the time.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	So then, in the first place, examine him to see if his oil is dry, hard, and free of any other disease but the scurvy;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then treat it in this way:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head in your shade, then hang down those that are close to the ground completely according to their wisdom, and let them be doubled up carefully according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two oils by degrees according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	and then carefully coiling those veins gently, and washing the blood out hour after hour, until you see those veins remove themselves from the oil.
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and keep the oil from touching the tips of the spatulas, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very hot in your work so that you only burn those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have finished this, let it distill in the oil clear and red wine to corrupt what is delayed in the sebaceous gland.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you do not have the power to coil all of this in that hour, then make a paste on the oil from soothing things that relieve the pain of the hair, and leave it for several days until the pain is relieved and is assured of the abscess being hot, then start again according to this method which is before until it is healthy;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of healing:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The wound is called a "fistula".
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you treat it with hot cauterization and medicine as I have said above, and it is not yet healed, then cut into the abscess, removing all the moisture as far as the bone, until the pain goes away.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed, and you will see corruption and blackness, then this is the treatment:
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "aspre chief", and be made of fire from the top to the bottom, and be pointed as a file, like this in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it on the site of the corrupt bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press with your hand a little until you feel that the corruption has been removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do not do this once, then restore the place of dry remedies.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the legs are closed and the back is straight, and the spine of the bow is also closed, and remains so for forty days, and he does not renew or get an abscess, and bad accidents do not happen to him, that he is well;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	if not, if there is no other way than to bring the fistula to the hole of the nose according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and that you uncover the bone the second time with iron, and with medicinal herbs, and when it is uncovered take it according to this form, and let the iron be at three angles, and the flesh be thinned up to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then put it on the bone with the saw of the lamia, and keep your hand away from the oil pot, then turn the whole iron until it goes through the bone and is felt by the patient because it touches his nose if he holds his hand on his nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and therefore restore the place of dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the horse has grown and hardened its limbs, so the material goes to the nose.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the oil issue
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are open in all directions, and it does not come to disturb the nose, neither does it decrease or increase, so you must lie the patient down.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then the healthy one, then put suction cups or a hat on to prevent pain from being sucked in, then put oil there, made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcolle, and then strain the oil, and plaster it with binders and cloths;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the method of the cloths is that you press cloths soft enough, and double each one in IV, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes need;
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then draw out from above a hard piece of wood, and start again the suction cups so as not to hurt themselves.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then take off the suction cups and let the oil be drawn out day and night, and if it becomes slimy, you must draw it out slowly.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then take off the ligature after day and night, and if you see that the oil is going back, it is good;
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	then start again with the plaster and the drape-like things, and the ligature and suction cups until it is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the breaking of a woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When the ruptures come in the woven fabric, then open, and comes out like a grain of resin, and is likely to be seen;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	So if you see it covered, the ovary is such that you push a needle into the root of the part below until it comes out, then push another needle where there is a double thread from the part of the armature;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and pierce her, and leave the first needle according to disposition;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut the thread twice and fasten a part of the thistle to the thread, and secure it well, then remove the needle and put on another damp oil in plenty of wax;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and let it be until the thread chokes with the thistle, then heal the oil from comforting things as long as the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and no time the wound is restricted by a thistle each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the hairs have great appearance, if it pierces the thin spatula which comes by virtue of the oil, and corrrects the moist albinized and cuts the hairs, and enters in so soon;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it as long as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bowels of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called 'alccunati' is only water that is mixed in oil, resembling water descending, and it is not water.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of the appearance of this chapter is that you should make the patient sit on one side with his back straight, then take the head between your hands from both sides and hold it up so that the hair comes to your fingers;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then place it in position, and do not let the light shine on it, and see the patient's things as if he were alone;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not fall out, know that it is sharp, and do not let the hair fall out from the head as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	if you sit the patient between your hands, then take the thin scalp and place it on the cornea with the continuity of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, until the hair comes out;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is out, pour hot sharp oil mixed with honey, or sharp or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then wash it with other washes until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	with the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have the appearance of arrows in division, and that which is necessary for piercing.
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	For in the work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your hands crosswise, far from light by the sun, and that you press the oil of st. John's wort very tightly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then place the paper of oil on your left hand if the hairs are on the left, or on your right hand if the hairs are on the right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your right hand, if the hairs are on the left, the instrument called 'almagda', or in your left hand, if the hairs are on the right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the point of the instrument at the root by its thickness on the pale side of the oil in the part of the lesser wound, then pour the instrument called 'almagda' with virtue, and turn back your hand so that it penetrates into the pale side of the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the measure of the vein of liquid gold be at the perfect measure of the space that is from the apricot up to the end of the blackness;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the crown of oil;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	so that you see the bone in this paper for the clarity of the cornified tissue, and then place the instrument at the level of the water where it is, then express it one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he is now awake, then the patient will see before him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	Then rest for a short time, and let the water rise again, place the instrument with force, and when it is firmly in place, if it rises, extract the liquid gold gently by turning your hand back and forth;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put a little of the clear water on top of it, and take out some of that oil from inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	And then take by the side the oil of spices or another wet in oil with a lot of honey, and bind with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those who are of our time, let us put on the komijn with a lot of honey.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the magda cannot enter into the oil by its hardness, because there are some men whose hairs are too hard, so it is that you squeeze the instrument which is called "alberit", from which this form comes:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce the conjunctive only a little bit, and do not go too deep all at once, but make a small hole, then pour in the liquid gold as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and for the completion of the work the patient prepares to lie down, seeing that he sleeps on his back in a dark place;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be free of all movement, and eat light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind it according to its position for three days;
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then lay him down in the same dark house and test his vision, and have him look at some things, and then bind it again for seven days;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not appropriate that you do this during the time of the cure or after the incision, but it is appropriate that you prepare him, for what happens to him suddenly in hospital.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	For the abscesses come up quickly, so that you take off the poultice before the seventh day and apply what softens the abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is calm, so that it does not see in the morning and put on its face a veil to cover any part of it, and be there in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then he left the house little by little, and turned his back on them;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no one should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us from the Land of Israel who told us that in our country it is used to eat almagre because it absorbs water, but I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancient ones;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	These are the appearances of the forms of almagre, so that he who does not know them may see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and let them be made of pure brass;
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of this middle subtility be, and behind it in three angles aigu.
de la char sor le neis	of the shoulder from the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	No one knows if these things will come out whole or half-formed, so some look like scorpions at the tip of the foot.
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	And if there are any of them that have a blue-green color, and if there is a red-brown color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In this case of those things that are red-brown, and not blue-green, you must place the patient between your hands, facing the sun.
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open their nostrils, and apply oil to those things, and massage them gently;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	So that you can hold the patient's foot in place with a thin splint from one side, until you are sure that the thing is all bone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there is nothing left that can't be covered with a thin, lightweight instrument, so that it doesn't stay in place;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if you do not mount on him, or an abscess, if the wound is as it should be;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is malignant abscesses, then you must hasten and cauterize as soon as the heat is withdrawn and all the pus is drained, then pour on it nor oil neither water nor wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	For if it is done, and moisture comes from there to the palace, know that he is healthy;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is bone rotten in the bone above, so that the instrument does not come to cut:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then you must put a thread of linen a little thick, and bind it with hands, and leave between each knot of space one or two;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient's cheek to the thread in his nose at some power, and draw it in smelling until it comes through the nose into the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times teach the child to go to school, and it is a light thing for him who does it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	and then hold the head that comes by the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes by the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart one after another like us who are spinning thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this as long as you can keep the thread from breaking, then turn the yarn, wash the blood away, and dip the yarn in Egyptian oil, and then put it back on the nose as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three or more days, until the oil corrupts all that is kept from being stretched;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put on the nose a string of leather for three days until it is well, and if it needs dry medicines, then use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, so that one infuses oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And be of silver or gold, resembling a lamp open, as a dog, and so lead them;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see, then make a closed bag, and be the instrument plain to purge the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and I always hold the head for him when one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the shoulder from the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease grows and increases in the head, and becomes great enough so that it is visible to look at;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and therefore you must cut it out at the beginning, and burn the bone thoroughly, then put fire or burning medicine on it;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you delay to cut it back until it is great, then take heed if it is hard, of the color, of the poverty of the sense:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if you do not touch me with iron for it is a infected abscess, because when one cuts it once, then there comes great evil to the patient;
