et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is due to a slow touch, not from a sharp pain, and you see that it can be covered completely, then empty the patient and let him rest in peace, and treat the abscess with dry things that will constrict and restrain.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	as the newborn is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is known that when a solution of continued nature enters one of these cartilage joints, it does so only slightly, for fear in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	So then, if there is any doubt, see if the wound is fresh to all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then join the two lips with a stitch, and then treat it until it is well;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are torn from one side to another, then it is necessary that you peel all their flesh until they heal, and then join the two lips together with a stitch, and bind them, and powder with powder of dragon's blood and burnt incense;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on the powders a piece of plaster of salt or other plaster that binds forever, and leave it until it falls off by itself, and then treat it with ointment until it is well.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The way of the wound so is that you bring together the solution:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or by needles, as we have said in the surgery of the womb;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	At home the apostem is hard within the lips, resembling grains of rice, and smaller and greater;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	Then you must turn the lips, and cut each notch, and take it with pliers and cut it into each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then employ fire after the incision of vitriol to scorch until the wound is stained;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then remove it thus, and treat the wound with dry things as long as it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times grow on the gums a sore that the old one calls "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	if it is necessary that you hold it with pliers and cut off at the root, and let run the blood or the sanc;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	and then over the vitriol water boil, or other powders restraining and drying;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if it returns after the incision, and often happens, so that if it is copped a second time, and cauterized:
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cauterization;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	are these forms of instruments for copping.
des sordens	of disorders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	No instrument is assembled to the head of the tooth, inside the mouth between the gums, scrapings which are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and the teeth are never black and yellow and rotten, as long as the corruption comes to the gums, and the teeth stink;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	So that you make the disease sit between your hands, and its roots are in your sanctity, and remove the teeth or scrapings as they appear, so that nothing is delayed;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and then you make it black and green, and yellow and other colors, until they are world;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if there is one bone broken, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, start again on the second day and the third, until you have all healed;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the teeth have different shapes of instruments to grind, according to what the practitioner demonstrates, and for those which the rasper whose teeth are grinding have other shapes than those whose teeth are not grinding;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others are arranged with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of pain that you delay the drawing as much as you can, for this should not be done at all;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because it is a very high substance up to which one has no excuse to draw it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Now when the patient is forced to pull, you must be certain about the tooth that needs to be pulled.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain makes the patient crazy, and he thought that the tooth was sound, and made him draw the good tooth;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and it does not remove pain from this, as long as the evil is extracted, because we have already wanted to do this with these gentlemen;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are certain of the tooth that hurts, then it is necessary that you scarify the tooth at all its roots; scrub it very hard so as to wear out the gums on all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then you put it on your fingers or with small needles at the first prick and prick, until it is well extracted, then you fasten the needles firmly;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the patient's head be between your knees, and hold it firm so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not fall out, take any of these instruments and put them gently inside each part, and move them as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if it is perforate and bleed, then it is necessary that you fill it with cloths where it pierces;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if the extraction is done carefully with small needles so that it does not break when extracted;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to make a bleeding over the gum in order to shake off the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be sure that you do not break it, and leave a part of it behind, and return to the patient with greater pain because of the root's mischief than from the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not do so as the ignorant surgeon does, who often breaks the jaw by his haste and boldness, and does not administer what we have told you.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but bring about by the incision of that great disease for the roots which remain, or for the chariot which they break, as we have often desired.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is pulled, wash its place with wine or with ash and with a string;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and let them heal from blood that often comes, for it often happens to employ the place of vitriol;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if this does not work, then burn with fire.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shape of the instruments, so that they do not damage the teeth first, should be long and thick, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be large members so that they do not bend when drawing, and made of good iron, and toothed so that they can hold fast.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root is wet while milking, if you place cotton wadding soaked in oil or butter on the joint for one or two days, until the joints are softened, then the claws which are called 'algefri' seem to be the cause of the problem;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and inside make it as with a file and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with all these pliers, you must uncover the jaw completely around the root, and put the instrument called "althali", that is to say a chisel, which is this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And be small and thin so that it does not break, and the root comes out through this, it is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if not, if you help yourself with all the tools, so that the forms come later:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has II rings, from which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front in the razory of the teeth, and this instrument which seems a pair of large pliers, from which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	and be the instruments small so they cannot break, and know that many of the dense instruments are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other tools, which are not worth counting;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the master subtleties try out their own instrument according to that which their work and the disease show them, for there are many diseases where the old teacher does not teach an instrument for the diversity of them; and if it does not break the cart or other bones, on which he sits, if he seeks the instruments that are suitable, I have told you, and help with gestures, so this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and firmly holding the bone, so that it does not escape but can hold and cut off.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the place of medicines that are right for it, and if there is putrefaction in the bone, and it is small, so the cure with all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not according to nature's form, and the shape is ugly, especially in young women, then you must know that the root is not in its right place, and it cannot be made sound with tooth powder or filing:
adonques lou raie;	then you shave
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it takes the tooth, then take this instrument which is described above, and which seems like a little fork, and make it of iron made:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cap is cut and cut with your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then file it with a file like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also as the file which one makes needles:
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and when I touch his tooth little by little, so that he does not move until he chews;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and then when it is smooth all over with a rasp, and its edges are too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, so it is necessary to sharpen the sharpness as much as possible until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth moves away from the jaw
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the tooth is loose in front, either by pounding or by chewing, and the patient cannot squeeze it without causing him to chew, and you have treated them with restricting medicines, and that does not work;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if they are restrained by a gold wire, because the silver thread becomes green and pus, but the gold does not move at all;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you can reach the back teeth, take the wire and bottle double between the two healthy teeth, then put the bridges between the back teeth, if there is one or more, until you have cleaned them thoroughly up to the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then start the cover again until the part where you are going to put it, and hold your hand gently and thoroughly as long as it does not move;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your lever at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then take the bridges with pliers, assemble them and place them between the healthy tooth, and put it in such a way that it does not hurt the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it tight as long as it can stay in place, and if it falls or the thread breaks, hold it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remains and serves this way for all its length, and this is the form of the bones and the appearance of their joining together as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth comes loose, if one puts it back in its place little by little, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and do not meddle with anything that is not skilled and tolerant, and never make the shape of a tooth out of yak bone, and put it back in its place where it fails, and hold it in place as we have said, and delay and serve thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the rings of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	No one should extract a tooth that comes loose from the tongue or nature, and do not try to put it back in;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a sore spot;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and put your hand on his chin, and pull back the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	And take the nerve with a broad hook as long as the tongue is dislocated from its position, and if there is pain or no pain, and this is sudden pain of wound, then he seizes the ligature and seizes the broad bandage.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and be careful that the incision is not too perfectly cut, so that the artery is damaged;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done this, lift up the water of rose and so on, or cold water, then put a piece of linen over the tongue;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and the poultice for each night, so that the ligature cannot be closed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if the blood flows out, then put vinegar on the ligature;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if it does not stop bleeding, then cauterize with the slow cautery, which is good for this;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then the doctor treats with other treatments until he is well;
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see a flesh-color that is black or hard, so that the patient feels it not, do not touch it at all, for it is cancer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining to blue-black, and there is moisture, then he gets the oncine, and makes it with a thin spatulum, and releases it from one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if it goes to your head, then put on vitriolic oil until it is burned, then come back to your head as long as you keep it all;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then raise your head and neck, and heal with other remedies until you are well.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	No one comes from within the throat that are called "gourd", and they are properly called "amandres", and when you cure them, as we have said in the section on dislocation, and they do not heal, then take care:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If the abscess is hard and of small size and pale in color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and its root is large, do not touch it with iron, either, for fear of the loss of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but you leave it until it is dead, and then you will remove it, or it would break by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of pale color and its root is thin, then prepare the instrument to cover it, but first see if the abscess is hot and inflamed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then you shall place the patient in front of the sun, and let his shoulders be level, and he should open his mouth and press the tongue against all the instrument, so as to form it thus:
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it should be of silver or of gold as thin as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	And when you have pressed the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the scaly and put it in the almond, and carry it up higher than you can.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and try to make any thread with it, then cover the instrument, so that this is the form, which seems like one force;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and all the way the head is corbeled, and one place to another, and are very hard, and is made of iron where or of adanie:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, take the cap with pliers, where there is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And be trenchant on one side, and on the other side no;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have covered one of the almonds, so cover the other according to this same way, and after the incision gargarize the patient with hot water, and hot and easily, and they move away from the blood if it comes, then gargarize the patient with water, or squeeze pomegranates that are cooked, or oak leaves, and similar things, until the sun is dried up;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then the treatment as long as he is healthy;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and there are no other abscesses in the throat than the two mandibles, if they are cut off properly like the two mandibles.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, that is to say, a small-sized abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had completely closed the throat so that the woman could not breathe through the constricted passage, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if she had remained like this for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had been misaligned by two rain-sized passages through which the patient had breathed.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	So I waited a little while, and then I put one of the oxen's horns in his mouth, and it tore at his flesh, and I pushed hard, and in a large portion of the bowel.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	and then I fixed another part in the other hole where the abscess was, and I wrapped his mouth, and pressed his tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	after I put the ringworm in these abscesses, and I drank a bit of blood from them;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and then he took out the tube from her throat and now he started drinking water and wine in turn, and did not stop cutting this abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess began to close again, and filled up the space that I had cleaned out, until it became very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I put a ringworm in it and cauterized it inside her throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	and then it didn't hurt anymore;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I left these parts behind, and only God knows what happened to me afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the uvula moves down, and she is running and distant, it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	And if it's big and round, it's called "uvula".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When she is healed as we have said in the chapter on division, and the healing does not benefit her, and you see that the foot abscess is quietened, and it is subtle, then you should cut it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is swollen and gathered is not far away;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or of a red or black color, then you should avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger with the eye disease.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its swelling and length, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press its tongue against the instrument of which we have spoken above.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then take the oncine [a type of hook] and draw it through the uvula, and trim it with two instruments which I have said in the chapter on incising the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the excess that is beyond the natural term.
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cover more, it will hurt the throat and the speech.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two amarets, and cure it until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear about covering, then you must use fire cautery on the sensitive parts.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the technique of fire cautery is sharp and piercing.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And that the patient puts his head in your lap, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we said or fire cautery, and mixes it with sharp vitriols, so that it is not too thick or too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and use this tool's manipulation, of which this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	and put a hair on one's head or a piece of cloth into the medicine, as if it were a spoonful of medicine, and place the instrument over all the medicine on the wound.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and let the patient lie on his side, so that he swallows and spits out the medicine from his mouth, so that it does not go down the throat and hurt the chest.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then take all the medicine in your hand and press it onto the wound, half the quantity every hour, until you see the wound heal and the medicine's bitterness ease.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see blood, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton with the medicine, and put the instrument all over the cotton in the bandage, until the cotton is wet all over the wound.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the burn has healed completely, then leave it to dry, and wash after three or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to clean the wound before applying the medicine, wash it first and then dry it. Take cotton soaked in the medicine and put it on the wound, and wipe away any medicine that is on top of the wound with a wet cloth.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be raised by cold water, and be cured by gargling as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, but only the cauterization.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is cured by fumigation in this way, take calamus and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and alfalfa and similar herbs, and put them all together or some of them in a pot, and throw it in, and let it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be very tightly covered with strong clay, and with a ladle stir it in this way:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	and of silver or gold, and let one of the bottles be put in the mouth of the sick person as long as the vapor rises to the nose through the tube, until the nose is deadened;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after this start often, as long as the nose dries up, and be careful not to do it at the beginning of the coming of the abscess, for many things come with it;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make any fire but to the declination of an abscess cautery.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, then take a knife and put it in the patient's mouth on the tooth with a hook, so that the fire does not hurt the patient too much;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	For the hook does not cause severe pain in the mouth, and this is good treatment overall.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Often there is an oss or a spine of fish, or nothing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so that you can see what it is, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing clearly;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and if it does not open and is pushed back into the throat, you must make the patient vomit in such a way that the food is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	in case the thing comes out by vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morcello
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and he takes an sponge and wraps it around his mouth, and then swallows it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the place, if it stays, and then you will pull hard;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out easily as we have said, then take an instrument of plunging according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be bent at the end so that it can enter more easily into the throat, and lift the chin up;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, that it does not block the way, and do not punch the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and show him how to blow out the instrument so that the thing is removed easily;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if the bottle is swallowed, or he draws it up evenly with all the instrument, as long as it is up.
de la sansue de la gorge	And be the instrument curved to the tongue so that it can enter the throat more easily, and lift the tongue high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that it does not come to the tongue, nor does it push the bone inside; and be sure that the patient swallows the instrument, for as long as he swallows, he should move or what is happening there; if the drink goes down, or he pulls the instrument back equally, as far as it goes.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No medicine should be given to him unless he has vomited it up, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when he does not benefit from it, then look in the throat of the sick person with the sun, because you press the tongue to the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, if it trails a tiny hook, or sharp claws that match this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if he doesn't respond, take a dog's chain, and pour it down the throat of the patient, then boil or simmer the blood of the dog, and make this happen often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is turning blue every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and dip it in, so that he swallows it, and moves it to his hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if soon after drinking the water he feels the bitter taste, let him spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not taste bitter as we have said, then burn the sick person with the smoke of the astringent, with the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the urine;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Make this many times, for she will not lack a taste of it.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the way of the smoke if that you squeeze it out a pot or it has coal in, and is the cover of a coverlet pierced into the middle, and in that hole where the head of the instrument is;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then pour out your smoke, and let the patient put the head of the cane in his mouth, and shut his mouth, so that the smoke does not come out but comes to the blood;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the blood will now run, and if it does not run, then begin again the smoking with many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and let the patient suffer thirst, and drink salty and bitter things, and do not drink water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it is necessary that she go out by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the form of the instrument has been seen to go out blood, if one can see it, resembling curved nails for them to enter the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and give it a smooth appearance with a file, so that whoever takes it cannot let go;
et vez ci la forme:	and give it this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the capsules of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Mouths of appearance are, according to whom the memory comes here after one and another in this book, and they are varied in piercing and cutting;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two ways: the first is in its own shape, and of what he holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	The second type are those where the location is affected.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Because the abscess at the top is different from that at the bottom, and the abscess at the charn (the jaw) is different from that at the joints, each has its own characteristics in terms of appearance.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if to abscesses one must not pierce at all, until the bowels are dead according to their accomplishment;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if to such as one must pierce when they are cured, and do not die according to their accomplishment, as is an abscess that has delicate joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses arise from the joints, and are left until they putrefy, there is a risk that the ligament and nerve of the joint may rot, which causes contracture in the limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or the abscess is a delicate limb, and if you delay the piercing until it is dead, it will harm the principal limb;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	Or it is delicate to cut down the root, if one cuts it in this way that it dies.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it does not seem to me that you pierce the anus after having completed digestion, so that the one who is delicate at the root does not spoil completely, and remains inside, and there comes a fistula.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and he cannot recover in great pain.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the time of piercing the anus which is dead according to completion, and that is when the pain is eased, and the departure of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the movement and the stabbing of the head of the anus, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make the piercing sit down where it is most dependent of the anus, and where it opens muscles;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the piercing of the long pipe, and if the abscesses are on the hands or feet, or in joints, and at the roots and arteries, and in all of them even, where there is no pleurisy.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases where they bleed, by what member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the flesh, if it is necessary that you leave the piercing until it is confirmed in the completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before this, if you lengthen the pipe of its blood, and it is full of filth;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance harden the lips and deepen the pit of it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to which the members have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you bring small abscesses, small pustules;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large pustules, and many splits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if for such abscesses it is necessary to cut the cure, and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when they are already become like cloth, and are deadened, so that you do the same with them as you do with blisters:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if they are cut into three angles, and if they have an opening like the skin of a mirth, like abscesses of arms.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if they are cut where one makes a round cut, and other cuts, and a similar cope.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	those who do not have a head, as in a superficial abscess, you must pierce it clearly;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and when the abscess is large, and it has a great bulge, and you pierce it, if you do not draw out all of the bulge at that time, but draw out a part of it;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess just until the next day, then draw out nothing therefor;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times from hard to harder, until all of the bulge is gone;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	usually the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman porter, or small children, or old honourable people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Those who do not have a head, like an abscess on the surface, it is necessary that you pierce it clearly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has a large amount of pus, and you pierce it, if you do not remove all the pus at that time, but remove some part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then remove nothing more; repeat this many times with great care, until the pus is completely removed; but if the patient has little strength, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old people who are decrepit.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Treat this text with great caution, and when you have pricked your abscess, if the wound has healed, examine whether the wound from the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a simple cut, then prepare cotton wicks or old cotton.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess and there are many openings, then you should place a wick in each one so that they touch each other.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut the skin around an abscess and sewn it up, then you should fill it with dry cotton or linen rags without moisture, and leave it until the next day.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, clean the wound and apply ointment as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is blood loss with the incision, then apply cold water and quickly, and wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the pain from the wound persists, then apply a remedy and cure as I have described in this book, and if it is an infectious wound, and the apostemes are very nervous, then you should place wet wicks and drapes soaked in wine and oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is not yet dried out, and its muscles are still soft, you must soak the fabric in water and oil or cold wine and oil for three days, as we have said before;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then wash away the abscess and wipe it clean and treat it, as is right, until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	This is followed by a discussion of how to diagnose and treat abscesses: "And this is how everyone should understand how to treat abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	or you have said before what one must do when going to the treatment of abscesses, and you will see the ink.
des soros	of the sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	or the little abscesses come out, and are handled so that they become threads, also like the joint of a thread, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There is plenty of grease and fat where there is moisture like poultry.
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And if it is such that they are hard and bony at the base, and there is no doubt that the artery does not oppose.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist so that you experience with all the instrument which is called "entrismoire", from which the form comes afterwards, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, if it goes up long way.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	When the moisture is dried up, if you do not leave hair on that part where the moisture was, because it will come back to place when you leave some behind;
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, in water and salve, and employ the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and those who have been delayed by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then begin again the cotton, if as before, the second day, and the salve, as long as you know that it does not remain overnight;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the wound with ointment suitable for it, until it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds only a little grease, if the incision follows this form, then let it be long;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and I will cut off your hair, and scorch all sides, and put all my treatment to draw out the cow's skin where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the arteries are opposed, do as I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also make of the abscess if it is bony, and of the cutting and curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on the bony abscess and moisten it, for it will be lighter in weight, because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if to some of these abscesses or head where there is no moisture, and of those that I kopayed in the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess just like a hard stone, sharp and pale, and could not break it;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if any of them had been cut, one would have made a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses that come out of the head, these are those that come at the tips of the ears and roots, the opening should always be made at the most dependent place so that the bow can be pulled out;
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat them as they should.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times an abscess comes to the neck, and it heals itself, and it leaves scars, and it never comes elsewhere or gets dry, and it is stinky, and it becomes infected.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scar is properly inside its rib, like the nose and the abscess on the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the appearances of these scars are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that which you see of good disposition in the chest, and is similar in color to the flesh of the body, and silent from each side and is not raised up at the neck neither at the artery nor at the vein, and is not deeply buried.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	if you cut it from the top, and peel off each part of it, and have the two lips of the chest united to one, if you need to do so, as we have said in the chapter on the chest;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and cut it little by little, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or the vein, nor is it too thin, so that your hands do not slip, and do not look too far ahead, so that you do not cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and it does not allow you to work, then put vinegar on the wound, or some powders that stop the flow of blood, and tighten the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscesses are calmed down, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood has stopped flowing, return to your work, as long as you continue.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	and then examine your index finger to see if there are any small blisters, if they burst and clean themselves.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is great pain at the root of a vein, it is necessary to cut that scrofula at its root, but to let it fall with strong thread, and leave it without any harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then employ cotton wicks dipped in Egyptian ointment, then apply the ointment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you have the whole scrofula, it is necessary that you gather together the two lips of the wound and sew them up, so that there is no delay because of its abundance due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is necessary that you listen to cover the root of it, and extract firmly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	These scrofulas that have a suppuration, pierce it where it is most infected.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce it as described before, depending on the case, then apply ointment and similar things so that those who are delayed by corruption are corrupted.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, if the wound dressing causes trouble, as long as it heals.
de squinance	from squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The old ones used to say and talk about the surgery of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw it done in our land, and that is from their writing from their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have laryngitis, the slicing of the throat which is called "epiglotte" should be removed;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	And let him not touch with his hands, for all the veins and the blood of the patient are in those who have an abscess warm in the mouth or in the throat or in II Amalies.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the hole of the vein, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis so that the strangle which comes from the constriction does not occur.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglotte, that we cut it with three circles or four a little slice from the side, between the two circles or by the quantity of the slice from the soft part; not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and if their lips are suitable for the cutting of the epiglottis that there is no carriage, and the vessel is long from then.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to its entirety, and then he cuts the meat as far as the chin.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then apply the balm to it, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and is proven by the cutting of the fluid of the chin that it comes out through the place that has been broken, and by the loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the open wound a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed by when one doubts about the strangulation, join the two lips of the wound to the meat, and the whole side is under the cartilage.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And administer medicines that cause a healthy birth, as long as he is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says: Don't do this as long as the throat is completely closed up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the deficiency makes it worse.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and to order the elder to leave the wound open as long as the evil of the disease has not passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then he ordered to sew up the wound and heal, until it was healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young woman take a knife and put it in her throat, and she covered part of the neck with her hair;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called by the healer, and I found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and I found the blood which was issuing from it, and I am sure that she had not cut a vein or an artery but rather the throat, and her breath was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, sewed up the wound, and healed it until it was well;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and not to the lady except that she was red in face, and returned after her own way;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for I fear in the cutting of the epiglottis there might be pain.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	An appendix is called "gastric hernia", and is a great appendix of a yellow color, and is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it has two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	natural and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	where the natural one has no pain.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one is according to two ways: one seems like fat in us, and the other way seems like an appendix that comes from our blood vessels;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and it has pain, and does not operate fire but in that which is small, and tests and searches all the intruder:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as well as fat, and cannot do anything, if it is cut, if it is like what we cut, and test all its hair, if there is any:
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well soon, and cure him as it should, until he is perfectly healthy.
des nous	Our
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways to do this, all of which I will describe in detail;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is important that I make the entire difference between what is natural and what is unnatural;
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that issue is painful and feverish until the boiling has passed and the purging is complete;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Then rest the fever and the heat;
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a natural recovery there is no longer any heat or pain or illness, and he begins to excrete, which is according to the color of his skin, and it starts like an egg, and becomes large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are according to two appearances, one fat or moist, and the other of various colors as I said in the chapter on division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to treat the body, you must first test and question all the instruments that are called "entromessoire", according to what their shape comes or the paste that is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the way to extract abscesses is that you squeeze the moistest part of the abscess that you can find, and turn your fingers in and out slowly, until you feel the instrument has penetrated the core, then adjust the size according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then take out the insertion tool, and be careful not to hurt yourself.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If there is a good moisture, which color it has, then cut it as I said with other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the insertion tool there is no moisture, know that it is greasy, so then cut it across and take it with pincers, and burn it lightly from each side and guard the cot where it lies so that you take it healthy with the nut;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot take it healthy, then take it in pieces so that nothing stays stuck.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if it sticks, it will come back to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it sticks a little and does not bother you, then employ some corrosive water powders on the wound, extract the wound, and put warm, soothing ointment on it, and heal other wounds until it is healthy;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and let us cut both ends of the wound, and heal him who caused this injury.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein is opposite or elsewhere, do not hurry and apply the fire of vitriol there, and leave it for two or three days until the wound rots, and rest the boiling of blood.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to copper that which has been delayed from the north.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of the intruding instruments, and they are three ways:
grans et moien et petit;	great and mean and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and they are of three ways:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	great, mean and small, so as to close up abscesses from fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles where sorcery is cut, and they are of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more proven by the ring blackened to close up abscesses from fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three ways:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	greats, mediates, and small ones, according to the quantity of the largeness of the apertures.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the incisors are of many kinds, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	greats, mediates, and small ones;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if the incisors that have two curbs of three ways also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if the incisors that have three curbs are also of three ways;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if the incisors that have two curbs, and some with only one curve, are of three ways;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	For the head of these to cut is sharp, and of such I have who do not cut but from one side, so that we peel the skin off, to cut the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these intrusives are the alems reposed in many, so that the patient does not get lost at the opening of the abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three ways:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and moderate, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and not use on but in the place of the neck, as legs, arms, mamelles, and armpits, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never does one make another instrument small, resembling to knots of fists, according to this form, so that it is not burned with fire;
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it no time to the place which is healthy for coping with veins, and arteries, and never again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	and never does one inflame the breasts of some men when they become corrupted, as much as they seem to be the breasts of a woman;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain lazy and swollen, and who wants to cure them, if it is convenient according to this form of these lines.b. until g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scorch the fat, and apply the wound with medicine, then join the two lips of the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	And if he spits it up, and it is thick because of its size, so that it resembles the women's breasts, if you cut it into two pieces from above, by two apparent cuts;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that the larger part touches the smaller one at the end of the one and the other, so that the greater line follows this form, from this line b. until line g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scorch the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply the stitches and powders we mentioned, and what else is necessary for the treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, so that the patient does not rest, or for the removal of blood, you must fill the wound with wet cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it remain until it has drained the remaining blood and fat, then treat it until it is healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	of the heels
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	The pustules that come from heel-spurs are handled in the same way as hard scrofula with ribs, and if there is moisture in them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.
