et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then sit the patient down on a chair, and have two small chairs where he leans his back and joins his feet away from the leg;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and that his thighs are spread wide, and place his arms across his knees, and bind them well with a good ligature;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then suck his baffle toward the right side of his throat, and I shall introduce the instrument with which one operates the mouth of the marris, from which comes the form;
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you see this instrument introduced, you stick a rod in first to test the depth of the marris, so that what enters the instrument does not come out more perfectly than it should, and does not hurt the patient;
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instrument is larger, then it should cover the end of the seam of the cloth so that the instrument does not damage it;
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it should put the tip of the instrument above, and dip the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess is opened, and one holds it with a wet hand, if it covers the top, to the spatumile lead;
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the bowel is empty, then you should put into the wound wet cotton wicks soaked in rose oil or dry green oil;
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and place the wick completely over the seam, and place it on top of the seam and on the other hand wet net soaked in water or cooked lavender;
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it after two days of ointment applied to this, until it is healed;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and never raise up the wound and disease by a warm bath of water and honey, and then of water or roots of licorice and arisolog long are cooked;
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	and then come back to the poultice.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound has healed over the marrow, you must beware of cooking with iron, but heal it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	It is first necessary for the midwife to know the signs of natural childbirth, and what they are when you see the woman rush down, and desire to smell the air.
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	then quickly the baby comes out;
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	then you will know that these births are according to natural order, and the first one comes out with its head, and the second one with it;
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, if it is necessary to press lightly on her belly, so that the baby comes out quickly;
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	for when he comes out with his head, the second one is with him, and the womb is cleansed of its excesses by good purification;
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and what comes from elsewhere does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it comes not at all on its own feet, and comes from the neck or shoulder, and the hands, or often comes upon its stomach, or sometimes turns upside down on its back, and is turned around by chance on its neck, and by other bad shapes;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	is a craft that needs to be wise and subtle in these things, and warn against error and deception, and I will show you all the shapes how one must help it.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If a captive comes upon his head through natural birth, and women give birth with pain, and its strength is weak, then the captor sits on a saddle, or women hold him;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and it rises up of oil or fenugreek that is cooked, and then pour the dance between its two little feet whose shape is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and split the second, and cut off his fingernail as long as the moisture that is spread out everywhere;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and rub the belly of the woman until the child is born, and if it does not give birth, then it is appropriate to rub the woman with mustard with oil of sesame seed;
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then let her rub herself and shiver with a warm compress, and keep her mouth and nose covered for an hour;
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	now bring the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if the two hands are cold, then it is appropriate that you bring them back together gently little by little;
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a chair, and lift her feet up;
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then take the chair off the ground, and stretch out the woman, so that she does not fall when she stands up;
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then put the knives that were placed before on her hands, and pull out the child, and bring it back together.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	the child's delivery from its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child walks on its feet, then it is necessary to raise it up.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it little by little until it is even;
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	and then stretch the feet little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Until it jumps just as high as its toes, then instruct it to bend, and make it shake with tremors;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps, then God help it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it doesn't work like we've said, then let it be slowly turned, as long as it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then he is lightly healed.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come as we have said, then take a small piece of ash wood, and oil of sesame, and gum that is melted, and grind it all together in an mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put this paste on the woman's breasts, then make her sit in fresh water until her breasts are soft;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	And when she is wet all over, then put a necklace of myrrh on her, and leave it on for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	and then set it on one side, then make it twitch and strain its mouth and nose, and pinch its belly lightly, because the baby is not born yet.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	the delivery of the child between its legs
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the baby comes in this way, if you put the hand on his back little by little.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then be careful with its neck, and let it hang down, and lie on your bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold his hands little by little, then pinch his belly lightly, and take out the placenta until it is completely gone;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the baby does not cry, if you stretch its legs and move its body, then turn its belly up, then put your hands on its belly;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and shake the child little by little;
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and tell the woman to lie down until the baby comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of a child who comes from the wide a hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to engage in bringing the hand back:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	If you can't bring it back, if the woman stands up and goes.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If she can't walk, if you make her sit on a bed, and stretch out her legs straight.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then arrange the muscles as I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she doesn't give birth, if you make her sit on a chair, and carefully try to bring back the arm;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and arrange the child according to its natural shape, and make it swing, and tell it to stretch as much as it can while giving birth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the birth of the child on his neck, and spread his hands, and turned his face towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	I think that the surgeon should wash his hands, then dry them little by little, and gently massage them;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, if you arrange the muscles as I have said, and oil them a little, then tell her to move little by little.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, if the fire sits on the seat, and commands that she is heated;
et la fai esternuer.	and make the fire shake.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	by this middle method to all the second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes in this way for a second time, if it is heated to the point of smoke, and the moisture is gone;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if it is put down on its face and on its neck, so that it is not held back, and the animal dies;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, as far as you have done it properly, and command the woman not to heat herself at all:
adonques si istra legierement.	then slowly;
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that good animals are often born, and never more than three or four at a time are born;
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and this is not a strange thing, and seldom happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and never live, if they are alone;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know this, that they may be multiplied, and are devised by the sage who devises them, who is bound to the bottle.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and never come naturally as we all do, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they are grieved, if the remedy is as we have said, and let the skillful midwife, and make quickly and lightly what she does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and make so as it seems good for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	And no longer are formed in the marriage I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more until XV, and all are formed in the form of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious, and know all this, for by chance similar things may happen to them;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so do as seems good to him.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat the woman of a dead child or belly, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are obliged to work with your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	If it is necessary for you to know that his wife is of sound health, and has no accident or she may die.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	If it is necessary that his wife be supported on her back, and that her shoulders are tilted downward, and her legs raised;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister is applied to both sides, or she is laid on a bed so that she cannot be treated for the delivery of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the pregnant woman with moist oil with mint and fenugreek and flax seed, then anoint his hands with these oils and these perfumes;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then pour into the vagina lightly, then take care that the baby is dressed and ready for delivery, and take care that the head of the fetus is not damaged;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	then insert the fingers into her vagina or into her cervix or into her mouth or into her palace (vagina) or into her beard or into her throat or near her ribs, and the delivery takes place on the feet, it is inserted or pricked and the ribs move;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and he should dye the oncine to his right hand, and put the corbel between his two hands with his left hand, and hold the oncine lightly in any of these places that we have said until it comes to the empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the form of the oncine:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then put another oncine there, where you need it, so that the extractions are even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then make them even by moving one way and the other, so that they come out easily, and hold the oncines' teeth firmly in place, like this:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	If one part stops moving, then oil some of its joints with oil and push it in that part, and pull the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if one part stops moving at all, put this oncine in a higher place, and do so until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot bring it back by the tightness, then you must wrap a blanket over him until it is all finished.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	Then cover it with a cloth in the joint of the foot or at the neck, and likewise you must do on the other hand, and at the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the child's neck is thick and in the birth it is twisted together with an acute bunch of thorns, then you must put the thorn-spasm between your two hands, and make the twist and extract the thorns.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you take the instrument which is called an almidah, with which the form comes out with the instruments or paste which comes after this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and likewise I make the child's deformity by nature;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then cut the bones with nails, and if the head jumps out and is held back by force, then you must split it, until the moisture that comes from its issue is dried up;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot be removed, then break it into pieces with a saw.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the abdomen or seeps from the sides, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if he fell on his feet, if the atraction is light, and the re-direction towards the mouth of the mare is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	and if it is stuck in the abdomen or in the breast, then you must hold it with a cloth wrapped around your hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and cut into the abdomen or breast until the moisture that is running out;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if another bone has been broken and the shoulder joint is stuck, then you must pull it out with your hand firmly around the shoulder, and draw it out up to the mouth of the arm pit;
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then you cut off the head or the foot, and you draw it out;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the arm pit is tightened by a hot abscess that has come there, then you must not move it, but treat wet and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and let them take care with poultices, and cut it with water softeners and moistening agents.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if he hurts himself on his rib, and you put it straight, so take care of what we have said about the living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if we cannot, then let him be torn into pieces, and leave nothing of the second.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, take care of what we have said about the feet that come out in the womb;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if the pain comes from there, then let it be put in water restraining, and take care of other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose child had died, and another consulting about that child, and another saying that the child was dead.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, the wound opened again and began to pour a lot of pus.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I thought for a long time, but I could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and there came out a bone, and after a few days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled very much, for the belly had no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I wanted to heal the wound, and with my own hands, until the woman was better;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and waited for the woman a long time like this, and it was a little bit warm in her;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I forgot about this paste until one day, when the master found a strange thing;
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to put the wife back in her place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Here comes the translation of the first sentence: 
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and to the two shoulders of the two lions.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be thinner than the head, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth should be two fingers wide, and the cheeks one palm and a half wide;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and the two limbs should be joined by a joint like this, which should be set at an angle of one palm's length or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two joints are fitted into the mouth of the mask so that they open when the horns are turned;
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another shape, more delicate and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of the claws;
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and it has two joints, like this, a palm' length long and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you open the woman on all the instrument, let her sit on the bed, the pieces up and the legs open, then put the two supports together in the machine, and hold the head of the instrument away from between her knees;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	and then open your hand to all the instrument, as you have done to the nails evenly, according to the quantity that you open the mouth of the woman, until the ball moves her so that she wants it.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	This instrument is all mounted up, and its appearances are multiple.
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when you see that they are prepared, the work is faster, and higher for men by their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair of the instrument unless you have prepared it, for there is no excuse for its lack of use.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	and when the second is ready to give birth, it is necessary that you order the sick woman to keep her tongue and then make her sneeze, and hold your hands to her mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she jumps high, it's good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	and if she doesn't, if I can catch it, and make a pit or bowl, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the mare, as calamus, rut, anise, chamomile, caryophylline, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or none of them, are cooked or put in water on the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then place a bowl or pit from the pot, and another at the mouth of the mare, and hold it until the vapours come out of the mare's mouth;
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If you miss the second time treatment.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if she remains after this cure, and is not better, order her to soak her left hand in oil of sesame or in musk-root infusion, and then pour it on the wound, and bandage it again;
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when she has found it, if she presses and extends it little by little correctly, so that the husband does not feel any extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but then it is necessary to move it lightly from side to side and then stretch it out;
si venra et se desaerdra.	so that it will come and dislocate itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the husband is tight and constricted, we have said the cure of stretching, and of smoke from herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if she does not follow all that we have said, keep in mind that you do not make a mistake when you stretch it out;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that the one who is at the mouth of the husband, you tie him to the cunt of the woman, and then anoint it with ointment of four-part herbal tar;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	so that he will sizzle and be reset, and will come out strongly;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but still, when she gives off a bad smell from the stomach and the head, and blights the disease.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	So it is necessary to do smoke inhalations suitable for this:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	neither of the old have tried smoking with dandelion and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument, to which you smoke the woman at the retention of flowers and the second one, is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And is like to a dog, and put the head lightly in the fire, and the shoulders wide upon the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the inhalations be on the coals, and the tan until it is spent, and begin again another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not yet had their navels cut, but the surgeon cuts them lightly with a sharp knife:
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	if it is necessary to dip him in water so that he cuts the navel of the surgeon with his right hand, and does not cut it at all with a spatel, and bandage him so that he does not touch it;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then dip it in wine and oil, then the cure of poultices until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not recover, then put a splint on it and leave it unmoved, and let the bone be exposed when it goes to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And never does a sudden blister come on a wound or an abscess.
si covient coper celui soudement:	if it comes to covering suddenly:
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	if so heal, if as we have said of the poultice of plaster.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistula which come from the fundament are nodulation, and grow heavier than those which come from the fundament disappear, or in the space of the II parts, if to one fistula or more;
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that nodulation is old, if it opens, and again moistens a bleached or subtle bow, and never are these fistula persistent;
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and are caused by what it is that he excretes or has wind when the patient makes excretion, and by chance in salt up one way.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if it pierces to a bladder, and just up to half of the penis.
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and reach only to the junction of the loins, and just short of the neck of the bladder.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And so recognize the fistula that pierces to the foundation, and not that pierces:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and is that you stick your second finger or foundation, and stick a small needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has curvature, if you stick a small piece of string or a horse's hair, as long as you feel the string or hair on your finger:
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you don't feel it, and there is no blockage of excretion or wind, nor does it cause pain, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	know that it will not pierce.
si te haste dou curer.	If you hurry to treat.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persisting up to the bladder or up to the conduit of the urine, if it does not hold the urine, and cannot be sustained with medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced only to the join of the thigh, then it comes back to its place only at the root;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no twisting and the pain remains in the entrails, then it is only at that moment that he should be treated with medication or immediate attention by feeling for the pain;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these persistent pustules there is no cure except work and vanity of foolish people who interfere with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In that which is not persistent and not old, there is hope of health by fire, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he lets his legs go up to his thighs, and has his thighs bent towards his abdomen;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then pour a little water, or if there is twisting, pour as much as you know where the pain comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels pain at the base, then you should place your index finger there, and feel that the nerve is being pinched.
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and so discover between your thumb and the syringe or cannula, then you know it is persistent;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it does not work, then it cannot be cured.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	By using the entire arm, one can perhaps cure some, but this rarely happens;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid that can be given, if one heats the small cauldron according to the width of the fistula, as it is said above;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and pour into the fistula as hot as possible without burning the base;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and make it two or three times, until you know that these needles are burned, which look like an owl's feather;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the healer of wet tents will cover them, as much as they want to cook, and then the healer of ointment will burn it and join it together.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If this happens, then it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	Or if not, there can be no cure;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if it pierces between, and not until the top which is at the foundation, and at the bottom of the tent a thick covering of tar or medicine, and you see the fistula to that person who covers from the medicine;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if the tar of the beginning of the fistula, and fastens to the tent, and then the cure after, until it comes to the top of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the tent will be delivered, and will be destroyed;
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then the healer of those who are burned will cover them, so that they seem like a goose feather, and there remain none.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound does not heal and a scar forms between you and the work, then apply fire cautery or bitter medicine to the scar.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the cure of fire brings together two things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	This is to know, the burning of these shoulders, and the tightening of blood and the drying up of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	and then he cures the tents that are wet, whether they are cooked or not, until the heads grow, and those shoulders are burnt in the fire.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	and then he cures the wound of the burning stones that have been stuck in the hard shoulder, and are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it has been restored, if it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes only to the foundation, and is distant from the heart, let him boil it up or at the foundation, and inquire that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tent, and come in between II is the cloth or medicine or stones, or is ready to pierce, so there is only a way of betrothal and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it just to the root, or if you can put tents on it and cure it as first;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not cut too deep in perfection, that you do not cover the fundament which holds the foundation, and come by the voluntary way;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	and then heal, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	in case it heals, or remove the covering and clean it thoroughly from its base, or with a towel or other instrument placed there;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then burn off that pus which is in the wound as well as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study to restore the wound and to delay the fistula at the edge of the fundament:
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is a lighter disease for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And in no way are fistulas formed in this way:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and when you cover the tent over the fistula, and it is at the edge of the skin on top of the fundament, if one takes a piercing towel at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I pour I thread tort in II, and pour the tent all the way in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it persists at the edge of the fundament inside, then extract the thread from that piercing, so that you cover your two or fundament:
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and turn the head of the hair, and assemble the two shoulders together, and pull them from each other, and leave it one day or two.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and do not restrain once, until the thread holds these keys that are between two, and they move.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound as long as it is sewn and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, if you make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is too much emparfonto
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not good to make a bandage tight all at once, and then to unbind it, if one wishes for the wound to heal completely.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the spikelet with thorns from which one does the tube if it is made of one, part and cut them off;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand not, so that we do not hold what we should not hold, if you see this:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	The emorodides are according to two ways:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are inside the foundation, as a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and cut it with a sharp edge, and there is one or more, and they are away from the foundation and at the top of the foundation;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those who are absent if there is little moisture, and soon after or a little yellow water or blood, and have the color of the flesh;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them in the fundament, so that you command the patient to sweat by going to chambers, until the fundamentals are gone, and the sebum comes out;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	so if you hurry, and hold it like claws, or if you keep it with your fingernail, then cut it at the roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the dislocation cannot be held due to moisture, take it with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of cloth;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them with your two hands, then cut them and powder them with any hot powders that are in the fire's place;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said or metal cautery, so they are cured with other cures until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if his foundation cannot come out, then cauterize the patient with the caustic and sharp clistere to wash away what is at the foundation, so that it can come out freely;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	When the patient is perspiring, and his muscles are hot from exercise, then the treatment is light.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and you should squeeze them with your fingernail or tweezers, and cut them off, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and do not incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	If you bring the stitch together in this way:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a twisted thread, and put it on a needle, then pull the thread through from one side to the other, and pass the two ends of the thread through the eye of the needle, and make a knot at the end;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and pull the thread tight, then tie the knot, and remove the needle, and do the same with all of them, and leave one for cutting away the excess blood;
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	and then place on the foundation I dip in oil with rose or in resin, and place on the foundation, and instruct the patient that he rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it for as long as it sheds, and when it is shed, if it is cured of the wound and other cures, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	and dry at the end or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often happens drying out at the end in the intestine, and by confinement of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If you are able to cut off at the point of a scalpel or with your nail the bark above, which does not leave it to moisten;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	and then treat it until it is healthy as it should be;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot harden, then begin to shave more strongly than before, until it bleeds and is scorched;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat it until it is healthy.
dou fremit	He will sweat profusely.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	FOMOZ [sic] is a small appearance of rot before the collar, and goes well wet perfectly;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and does not cut the vein, but feels like he is dead with a shiver, and enters all over the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a feather from an egg of a goose, or a feather from a strong vulture, and put that feather on the shiver, until the purple circle completely covers the shiver;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand over all the feather until you have covered the entire shiver, and put it on perfectly, and scratch the shiver from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, then make this of a dog's or a horse's tooth according to this form and be careful with the sharp edges and let it run over.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	do not cut, but keep holding onto both, and press.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see this, cauterize the shiver with fire, as it is before or with the chapter of fire to cauterize.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the 클리스터
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Do not do this, but make a silver solution, or iron solution, or melted gold, or milk;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and never do these instruments small or large, according to those to whom they are brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	So it is that one brings for the cure of children and who are weak and painful, are small ones.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clister is small and big if above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	I have seen a distention where the belly is tied, as you see it, and the legs are pierced inside.
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and one of the sides has an opening, and the other side does too;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the belly is filled with medicines from a skin of wine or parchment, and all the small openings are pierced, and between each opening there is a space, then tie this space strongly with a sharp thread twisted in an X shape or a loop around it, and sew the belly together like a sheepskin;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, if the instrument has a strong thread before it, then sterilize it;
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	this is the shape of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	and it should not be too hot or too cold, and oil or saffron oil or some other thing is smeared on the head of the cautery, then pour it lightly;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	Then the ministers take the cup in both hands until it is completely full, and then pour out the medicine for the patient while holding his legs against the wall, and let the medicine come out as much as possible.
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a whole night, that is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize him because of a decay of the stomach, and the medicine hastens to come out, then remind him until he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if his hemorrhoids are in the foundation or abscess, so is the clister as subtle as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and that is the form of the clister subtle where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	Or we will tell you the cures for hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that there are various wounds according to what they are made, and according to the places where they are made, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the hitting of a stone, and the cutting of a sword or a knife, or a lance or a staff or a mace or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	where are made according to the rules of the body, such as a wound that climbs up the neck, or on top of the head, or breast, or abdomen, or liver, and similar limbs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, beginning with simple wounds on top of the head, because the reminder will come in this chapter's paragraph.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes on top of the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from falling onto stones or similar things, and the skin is already torn and the wound is large, and you wonder about the warmth of an abscess:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if the fire begins to warm the skull in a few days if it comes from blood loss from the wound, and if the heat is opposite to the wounded part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and the patient's appetite for wine and fatty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not get better, or his meat is reduced, and he does not drink wine, nor eat cheese.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put a warm cloth on the wound, if an abscess forms, cotton wetted in oil and applied immediately, or in wine of cypress.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess, if the wound is fresh and does not move with the air, powder, which I will call a little later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the fire has moved it, if he puts some onions on it, until he is cured.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great as of a sword-blade and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tension, if they are brought together by stitching, as I will say to the wounds of the belly, from the stitchery.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is open and deep, and narrow, and only a little, then the wound.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then heal the wound with medicine, and use hard leather instead of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meat, such as roasted meat and cooked grain, as well as poultry and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a boil, and it is not to the bone, then cut off all of it, and pour in water, and then treat him.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if he has an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped with binding, then cut the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then re-align it like a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not benefit, then burn it with fire.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the light cure is appropriate:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and that you put this powder in it so that the wound heals.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the method for this powder is:
pren encens une partie;	take incense a part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	and dragon dung II parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	burn alive III parts, and the powder gently, and apply to the wound, and bandage it tightly, until it heals well and joins together all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then let it lie well, and leave it unbound, if it doesn't swell.
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one does not bandage the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should one use live chalz solely, except when one has incense or dragon'blood, but fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the burn has moved the wound, at least put on it this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on certain oil extracts or meal of barley flour made with water and honey until it stops itching;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pinches;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound at the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is at the throat and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but the artery at the throat is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is asleep, if there is no other way to leave the cure than to put something restraining on, because it hurts the sleeper and makes him retreat;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the extension of water is with the brain, which is the highest limb.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	But the medicine should be warm, as hot water in fresh water, and mixed with rose oil, and boiled too, in fresh water, and other stones of different sizes according to this method, and moistened with oil.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then bind it with strips, and then treat until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and full of pus, then pierce or cut deeper.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and the blood flows out, then stop the bleeding, and cauterize as necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the course is blocked, so as to make the meat go down, then cut the wound on the chin of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then maintain it restrained, and leave it for some days, then treat it with onions until it is healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then seek it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, and you cannot take them out completely, then leave it until the wound festers and comes off on its own, and let the discharge run as it will;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound, and there is an fistula, then treat it as I said in the chapter of the ointment.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	if it is a lance or sword cut, and the wound is deep, then look out for wind from the wound that causes the patient pain:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	then know that the wound is deadly;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep and is fresh with all its blood, then do not put on the powder at first, nor bind it so that the blood does not run fully, and turn to the side, and let the patient rest;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I have a painful sensation, and I leave it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you have no pain, put cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if you do not get any spasm, nor a bad tremor of the heart or extraction of bones;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal this and other cures, until it is healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot be healed, and it continues, then know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	if the cure is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or a knife, and it is simple, or more or less deep, then the cure of this one;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	s’elle est grands, de couture;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if they are large, of sutures;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not relieved, then let the wound fester, and make the extractions lighter.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other members is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Dou derrompement dou ventre
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The breaking open of the abdomen is great and painful and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from a great wound there does not sometimes come out the intestines or where they lie, so that there is an insertion of air;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the suturing is more difficult, and there is never less pain in a small wound than in a great one, so that we put the intestines back together only little by little, putting them back together slowly;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	so that the intestines swell sometimes so that they feel cold, then we put them back together more slowly, and because a small wound heals more quickly than a large one, so that we keep the intestines in place until the others;II.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four ways:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common sutures in the belly wound are in the stitch of the other wounds of the body and the two special sutures are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and all of them are more proper with the stitch of the belly, and I will tell each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine comes out, and there is no need to wait for anything, it is by one of the four ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen with the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is hot, warm it in the fourth way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	Soak a sponge or a linen cloth entirely in warm water, or cook it with lukewarm water and saffron and aniseed, and drain the intestine until it swells;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and never did this wine causing restraints, and is muda that I soul for dispel.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is moistened with water or salt and cooked meat is heated, for by this is the entrance of little things prevented;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small hole in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is to make the person quiet, so we should not cut them unless there is great necessity;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	This is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	If you split it inward and not outward, and see this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines are protruding, if you can put them back in their natural place in their proper position, for that is difficult.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower part of the loins, then you must make the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part of the soul the belly, so put the chief and the penis higher than the parts of the soul, and so too the opening of the belly is in one of the II parts so put t'entente in this that the part navrée be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and so it is necessary to administer what I say in great wounds and deadly ones.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds put what you are equipped with, then put between your hands pitous who darkens all the opening at its hand, and close the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common way of sewing on, and it is that you press a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the chief of the wound I space of ii inches, and I stick a needle or he has i good thread;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the II skins of the skin inside, as much as you make it pierce from that part, and assemble the II chiefs of the siphac together, the three together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then the extraction of a double thread from the needle from both sides, then assemble the two heads of the wound in front, and then leave a distance of two spaces, and put another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	and then the thread is cut as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you need with the needles until all the wound is closed;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be small and large, because small needles go through all the fabric, and too large ones cannot enter well;
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	so that they can be made smaller;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and do not put the needles too far from the fabric and the leather, so that they go through and open the wound in front of the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cover the heads of the needles so that they do not burn the patient while he sleeps, and put tents or sheets over the heads of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is closed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of sewing with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because it takes a needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common, and is that you join the two pieces of leather and the two pieces of cloth together with a strong thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced these four together, then take the needle to the part where you began, in the manner that we sew clothes;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place a space of about the thickness of a smaller thread between each stitch;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch is suitable for a home-sown wound or an abdominal injury that has been cut with a knife; it was about two hands' widths across and contained intestinal tissue about two palms' length long; the wound ran into the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine then it had been outside for XXIIIII hours, and the wound was closed after XV days, and I treated it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the miracle was that he died, and this was a wonder;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and do not cure it with ointment, for I am in a place where there is none, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and put on cotton wool over the wound twice a day, and rinse it with honey water until it was well.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Or I will tell you the two proper ways to sew:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and thread it from the outside in;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the flesh on the right side in line with the injury, take the thread that you have threaded through the eye of the needle and let it come out at the opposite end from the surface;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the meaning of this stitch is that you sew as the furrier does when he makes fur, and leave a turn on one side, and take it up on the other, until the stitching is complete.
