Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of sewing, as Galenus explains properly, if it is so, as there is no font, who join the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the heads to the other head, in this way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	take an eye or head near the mirror next, and make it pierce that only, and leave the two heads of the syringe;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part only to that inside, as two heads of the syringe;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other from the outside part only to that inside, in two other heads of the mirror that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and that is the method of sewing and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galenus says this word, and no one testifies, that we must sew the belly to two needles, or there is a thread in each;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one needle from one part, and the other from another, in the manner of those who sew leathery;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the rupture is inside the belly, then the縫合更痛 than from other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound if they are such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and is that when you find the fresh wound to have all its blood, so that the meat has been moved by it, then put back the intestines and the cut.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on the powder in preparation for closing, and if the meat has been moved by it, then put on any ointment that is available, as long as the wound bleeds;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and chop the thread, and let the needle be heated and the wax;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with others until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you don't have medicine, put on it, until he begins to go away bowels, cotton wool, and stir twice a day as long as it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the main members, then it is appropriate that you moisten another light part in oil of tempere hot, or in oil of roses, and put it around the joints, and clean the blisters;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if it feels pain or irritation in the bowels, and many times happens, if the blisters are washed with black wine, and most likely the irritation comes to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot be healthy when it is newly born, and this is because of the location of the veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and because its nature is close to that of a newborn.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the wound oozes, then put it back as well as the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has become black or brown, then the place that is black should be cleaned so that blood does not flow from it, because there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then clean what is between the link, and hang the two shoulders from the side of the wound to the end so that the extraction can be done when the wound oozes, and the wound is closed.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine has been torn, and the wound is small, then it can be restored in some cases, for I have seen honest men whose stomachs were pierced or stabbed by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and there was vomiting and diarrhea;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I will use my skills to heal you as best I can, and I will not stop applying treatment until you are well, and let the wounds heal on their own.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw that the wound was healing, I doubted that the patient had done harm to his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but delay in good conditions, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they said no experiments that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied with some sort of ligature:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	Take a thin piece of wood from a large tree, then bind the lips of the wound together, and when the piece of wood has opened the mouth, place it on top of the two lips, so that it can extract its mouth:
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then he covers the head with it, and stays like this so that it cannot be undone, and puts another piece in the same way in front, until the wound is completely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and cover the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If this occurs in the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, and can be tied with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the end of this thread of intestine which has been cut off, and then tie it to the end of a thin twine of linen, then tie the thread around the skin, then cut the intestine, and then pull it back at the incision.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of sewing with threads is more secure than the way of sutures and faith.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestine's grooves, there is no need for sutures, but care must be taken.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or where it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	That said, all wounds and abscesses, once they have healed, are called "fistula" in general, and most importantly when they have scarred and closed up with a hair-like thread.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the green nodulation which is hard and blistered, or there is no pain felt, and it is also soft like the feathers of an owl;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and never by clear bow, and sometimes thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	never punch, and sometimes strong enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no cure, it is only because of one of VIII causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by small blood or pus;
ou por sa malice;	or for his wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because something hard is inside it, and on the lips, which does not allow anything to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or where there is too much bow;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or where his bones are rotten, and the material is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or where the medicine is not good for the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is in the manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or where, for property, in the region there is late digestion, and late health, and escapes by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins where there are bones
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have briefly described all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or is necessary that I make you aware of the cure for fistula, which is made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all limbs of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	For fistulas come from all parts of the body; because they occur in large veins, arteries, nerves, or the uterus, intestine, bladder, any of the ribs, spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes from a limb that is primary to the body, and similar things to the root.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas of this type are of great difficulty for treatment, and there is only travail and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is no fistula that does not come to the surface, for which you have begun treatment and which you can clearly see, then take a piece of leather or iron, if the fistula is straight, feel along it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if it is twisted, so the hole of a thin probe dip, because the dip bends much inside the twists;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if it is very broken and you cannot well search it with probes, if it is cleaned by one of the breaks, because moisture comes from one break to another and cleans it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and then examine it with your skill, so that you know if there are bones or nerves, and chop them completely, and ask the patient to feel the pain that he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you really know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or any of the places that I have told you, cut it according to what I have told you, and take out the broken bone and the corrupted cartilage that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure as long as it is healthy, and its fistula is very deep from the right place, so that you cut it completely, as much as you can, then put wet patches in medicine water, and bottle them up to the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the excess that is delayed at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put ointments in a clean cloth, as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackening, then cut it down as far as the corruption goes, then treat with ointments in clean cloth as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if he is not healed, and return bow as before, know that you have not yet come to the end:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it reveals itself and seeks out until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if he is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	if not, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot come there;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to relieve it by nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is one little bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with pliers, if you extract it with the right instrument for this, and if there are many bones, then pull them out all at once, do not leave any;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture makes it opposite to you, and there is no mistake or fear, if you put it in moisture and dry it, and deliver the bones;
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you do not remove them in an hour, then put on the wound something that provokes rot, and let them rot around the bones, and then the bones will have less difficulty.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as the leg or thigh, let the corrosion continue until the blackening covers all the bone, and then close the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if it is a great deal of corruption, and comes up to almost the end of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then cover all of it with poultice, and then treat it until it is fixed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about a case that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take an example and help from this teaching.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man of around thirty years old who had a pain in his leg from an unknown cause, which caused the matter to come out of the leg, and there was a large abscess, and he had no cause for it to open up;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the mirrour by their madness overran so much that the abscesses opened, and they corroded a great deal of matter, and became a fistula, and it came to pass so much that all went bowels and moisture from the heart;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many I cured within two years, and there was no cure for me in the art of surgery, until I was called away, and I took my leg and the medicines with which they were treating it, and that which ran through the perforations to the heart;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and his body became red in the youth, and had an orange color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I put a tent in one of these apertures, and then searched all the apertures, and found that one came against the other on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	So I hurried away, and I probed into one of the perforations until I discovered part of the bone, which I found corrupted and broken, and the corruption went up to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I knew what was corrupted in the bone, and I took care that there should be no other corruption, except for that which I had already found;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with medicines that are long lasting, and cannot be bound.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I discovered the bone as it was before, and I found that there was continuous decay in the bone, and the socket, and then I removed the socket, and then I leaned to bind the site;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not as I cupped up with my hand a palm of the bone, and I took it away completely from its socket, then I restored it with medicine;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and he was healed and bound tightly, and it did not need to be reopened for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Car for the evacuation of blood often, but it was completely healed, and gave birth in place of the bone a hard shell, and was of good disposition and did not harm nor opposite from all in all, nor air nor come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place of the spine, then it should be done in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take a bandage, and strain it at the top of the bone that is open, and do not command anyone to stretch it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and if there is another piece of string thicker than the first one, tie it over the joint that has come out from behind the bone, and pull the loose end of the string to the side so that the thread does not damage the joint.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and if there is a stick or a wedge behind the bone to move it back,
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to continue sewing as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and sew again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corroded and does not close up, and the corrosion is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the whole joint.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then put a stick or wedge behind it, and sew the corruption from one part to another, and let the thread go out of the long side of the corrosion, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cover the corrupted joint and sew the bone where it joins from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if it is corruption in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other pain than that of copper.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if it is corruption where the hand grabs, or where the foot grabs, then that is very strong. However, you must inquire about this corrosion and how it hurts you.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve does not make it contrary to you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incisor and the sutures to copper these bones are many, according to the placement of the bones and the appearance of the teeth, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this it is necessary that you prepare your instrument according to each of these needs;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument that you need, according to the knowledge of this craft and the testimony of the ways of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you will use the instrument with which you are skilled according to what is necessary.
dou feu	Fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The joints might be dislocated due to pressure or due to movement.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have medicine that can corrode by the cure of medicines, and it does not benefit, if you cover that member to the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes from death by the fault of the member, which is greater, from the wickedness that causes it;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the members become black, so that it seems to be burned by fire, and after that blackness, this corrosion of the member takes place from one member to another, and covers all the body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if you hurry to cover it, and if it is by the stinging of certain poisonous beasts, such as scorpions of the sea and snakes, if the corrosion is at the top of the two joints, if you cover it, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes to the hand, so that the cap goes to the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, so that the cap goes to the shoulder;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and all this while that the corrosion comes or stops:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes in the first joint, so that the cap goes after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes or stops, so that the cap goes all over the place;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises up the leg, so that the cap goes to the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to make the sick person die by the slow motion of the corrosion;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the way of capping or sowing the member is that you bind it above and below, and extend one minister between the two bones with a long nail, and another minister the other bone with a long nail, and you remove the cap which is between the two ministers at a large spatumile, as long as the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And then take a silk cope, and put of each side a cloth of linen, so that the silk does not touch the sound place, and thus come to the patient another wound and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding comes when you work, then cauterize the place promptly, or put on some powdered restraints;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your medicine until it is finished, then bind the limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened at home in a little while:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	he had a blackness that seemed like fire-burned, and this corruption came first in his foot due to the stone, so it blotted out all of the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the honorable man saw the corruption, he covered his foot with copper, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long ten after he came the corrosion or two of the hand, and came to me, and I put him on things responsive after the purification of the body, and can not stop the corrosions;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he said that I cut off his hand, and I did not do it, but I had hope to reflect the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and doubted also that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, because the virtue of man is weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he was despairing completely, and returned to his land, and he got well by copping his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I do not tell the story but that if one does something else, one should do it well.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Now and again comes an abscess in the swollen part, and holds back so long that it causes great gathering of bowels;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then run and pierce, and jump out of it, and stay in place your eyes, as well as our servants;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is above it is also very thin like the threads of a tapestry, and does not run into the bone, nor into the nerve, and such disease is called "san" and not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it gets so long that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin if you cut all around it, and most especially when it is thin like a tapestry thread;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not burn because of its corrosion.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	If you have promised that the skin will burn, and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thin like a sheet of leather, so you use this treatment with it:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look if his breasts are large, and the breast that they have is of a foul smell, then let him be treated with Egyptian medicine that is made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take ajar, and oil, and leadite, evenly, and put to cook in a vase on the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take of this according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and clisterize his breast, and extract the pit;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for two hours, then remove it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this muting time, until the breast is completely broken, and the pucker is made;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and no time is treated with water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you squeeze ashes from a vine's wood, and pour water on top, then let it flow, and treat it with, until you know that the breast is completely broken;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, neither Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, if you cauterize with water and honey or a little bit of lead oxide crushed;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you cauterize with honey and wine, that the honey has the property to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the wound stink;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you have assured yourself that the breasts are well cleansed, if you cauterize with that which causes them to grow, and it is that you press an ointment definitively, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cauterize with certain medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken in treating of ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the nipple is small, and the cautery knife cannot enter, if you widen it a little with an iron bar, and put in it a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicum ointment, until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too wide, so that the pus comes out so much that it can enter between the cup and the skin above or below it.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the boil is round, if it does not burst in the middle.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cover the breast as you see, so arrange it in such a way that the boil runs to the lowest point; for when the boil is round, if it does not burst in the middle, and if you cannot cover the breast as you see, so arrange it in such a way:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the boil runs lightly down, and do not leave any of the boil;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take medicines that solidify it, put it on a linen towel that covers all the breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cover the hole on the breast from the other side as tightly as possible according to the quantity of the hole, and put it over the hole on the breast to tighten the boil, and do not take off the large towel for a long time;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and those who are out of the breast of the heart, often for the purpose of extracting the bowels, and know what runs from the bowels, whether it is poison or pus or enough or digestible or undigestable;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and how much medicine has been spread out in some way and you see the nature that rises up on the breast of the heart, know that the breasts are already sore, and approach the sanctity;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then take off the dressing in the morning or third day, and when you dress the wound, if it is another cloth, and renew the poultice.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if her breasts become swollen and uncomfortable after many days, know that her breasts are not yet ready.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poison becomes evident after a long time, do not despair of health because health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are some who are late in wetting their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the digested bowels rise up out of the heart after many days, know that the breasts are not sore;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if it is delayed in coming out, and is prolonged, so take medicines separated wet in substance and dried in virtue, as the remedy definitely finishes, for there is a great part of vitriol, and this is the behind medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take the separated remedy definitely, and make it with oil rosin, and dye it with uniform red wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then make it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and this itself is made better by cooking, when the separated remedy is not present, or you take mirr and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on honey when it is out of the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then pour it in a dripper, and put it on the breast, and never administer it with wine long time, and roots of the celestial plant, which is also like flour of times and hundred;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in simple medicines or compounds:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	crush them, and make a powder, and put on honey that I have said, and use;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the cure is long, and this cure does not work, then know that corruption has taken hold, and causes pressure in the bone, or in hard members, or in limbs;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of the cure of the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the toe of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Paraclete is a wound that opens at the nail of the hand or foot, or perhaps opens in another two;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is sent, and no attention is taken, if it comes to the root of the nail, and perhaps коррорти whole;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes to the bone, so that it causes a painful ache, and the two fingers are wide apart, and the color turns blue;
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, then you must cut off all the excess that has been reserved of the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The fire cautery is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses into the flesh, and begins to prick, and bleeds, then you must cut off the nail that pricks the flesh, cut it high up, and carefully and lightly chop off the end of the nail, and put burning and corrosive medicines on it to stop the bleeding;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then you must cure it with onions as long as it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then chop and grind it hard, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the bone getting corrupted, then cut and grind it as described above, and then cure it until it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is broken, burned, and smells bad, then you must heal it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the nail of the spittle with a saw in a cross manner above, and be careful that the saw does not go beyond the nail, for otherwise the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if so, put something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	La douleur du sourdoit de la main
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Le doigt qui pousse dans la main de certains hommes est entièrement charnu, et par occasion il y a un os, et jamais une ongle, et aucune fois la racine de la jointure nait dans aucun d'eux.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Whoever is born in two different places will not move, and whoever is born at the junction of two places may move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The saw of the chubby one should be light, like this:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it with a large nail at its root:
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Whoever is born in the root of the junction is hard to treat:
si te tien dou coper.	If you hold it with a lid:
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In whoever is born with an odd number of legs who must be cut off at the hip: first cut around the hip joint neatly up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable knife, and finally treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together in two pieces are those that, by birth or by injury, or by fire's scorching, or similar things, come to be.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you cover that one with a lid so that he can be repaired according to his natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	and put between two tents or drapes wet in oil rosin, so that they do not stick together:
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or place between two thin pieces of wood, as long as the logs are tight together, just as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	She begins to touch any of his two with the palm, so handle it like this is right.
des vils	of disease
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The vis are great wrapped up envelopes full of melancholy excesses that come from many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more comes in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry, which is others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should not give him any kind of purification treatment, and then cure it from the base of the nose.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The cure for this in two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that they are copped and the black blood is drawn out;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cut is done according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	first the leg is cut with hot water so that the large vein is thin, and then it is extracted from the leg of the sick person up to the hip joint;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then the vein is cut in one, two or three places, of a large size, then it is drawn out and black blood drawn out by hand, from one side to the other, as much as the patient can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then let it sit, and he orders that it be dipped in black pepper meat.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and then start the evacuation and salting when the veins are empty, and rub on the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The treatment is done in this way:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Rehearse the leg of the sick person, if there is hair, then put it in bath or dip it, and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red, and swollen the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you do not have a bath, if you heat it at the fire, and then apply hot meat to the vein at the heel of the ankle, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then soak the skin with vinegar, and scrape the vein from each side until it is smooth when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it turns red and black, and when it enters or leaves the skin it seems as white as a cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	and fill it with water as long as it is lifted from the skin, and then put it in the oven at a low temperature, and then cover it with a cloth over three days.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	and burn the skin on the vein as long as it appears, and then remove it from the fire, as you did, and put it in another oven, as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	and cut another piece, or more than you need, and then remove it from the fire, and then wrap it around the second size of the stone, and then trimmer and remove it to the second size;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	and extract it piece by piece until it is completely removed, and then wrap it up;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot pull and lift it, put an extremely sharp needle on both ends of the thread, and tie and cut it, and fill it with fire, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and make sure she does not break, because if she breaks, neither can we pull her out nor lift her up, and this will harm the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have treated it completely, place wet wool in wine and oil over the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the patient heal.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if it is twisted and bent and wrapped up together, and is not straightened, as we have said, then you must split it in a twisted manner, but do not cover it;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have described above.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of the iron which you cover over the joint should be curved, and do not cut it off, so that it does not break the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it should be thickly curved, for if it were thin, it would break the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in legs, warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and soil that is dry.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And sometimes it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this comes from a sore that cracks the skin, so it goes inside the body, crawling between the skin and the bone.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that an extremely great inflammation comes in the leg, then the places change, and it begins to come out of its place, just as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head is open, if you wrap a piece of linen cloth from one and a half to two inches in diameter around it, and then close it, and leave the cloth attached to the leg, and every time it comes off, as soon as the cloth comes off, and wraps it back on;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too far away, then wrap one part of it and cover the rest, and do not cover its root entirely until it is completely covered;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cover it, then it enters into the bone, and brings an abscess and sores where it is, and a bad disease;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for that thing it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the root, and there remains nothing or wound.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and it is never this vein when it is treated with the palm of a hand, or ten fingers, and one hundred [people] die for me, at whom she stopped from ten fingers long, and when you cut her, if it rises or falls, and pierces up to the base, so that all is broken;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and be empty the matter that is within, and bring to its place medicines against putrefaction every day, then heal it as you do with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	and never this vein when it is opened in the joint of the foot or the leg, and it comes out with great pain, and where there is much swelling;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	then heal it therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	The hair should grow between the hide and the horn;
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "beef disease", for this it often enters the bulls, and is a small worm that births between hide and carriage, and goes all over the body up and down, and feels well to one member after another, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and leaps far.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And is infected with pus of some humors, so that it comes towards them, crawls and glides and worms or maggots in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	And there is doubt of its maliciousness, for when it goes through the body and comes to the head, and comes to the brain, by chance enters and destroys the brain.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him being cured and drained, so can't one force but when he goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	So it is necessary that you lay him down on a strong bandage that is tightly tied up, then cover and drain him well, and the liquid comes out completely into the carriage, and you do not find it, so burn it with fire, until he dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greater harm it does, if it corrents the oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see the head coming towards the oil, then restrain it by its neck form; and strike him hard; and
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and use the patient of medicinal solutions to rid the bad moods from corruption, and wash with meat that is rotten with corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some limbs, and moves from limb to limb;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I uncovered her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and I poked after, and I saw it rise up as a worm to the shoulder, more quickly than anything else, so as a lively silver when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain leaves that place, and enters the shoulder, and then after a little while corrupts all the body, until it comes to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	and then he told me that it turned again inside the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled at how this woman moved her member from one to the other, for I have never seen such a disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I have seen many who wanted to move their pain from one place to another, but I do not want to see it, as I saw it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that was because her torso was very thin, and the veins were exposed, and because it seemed that the wind was forced out;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear to me according to this reason for those who are healthy, who have moist bodies and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you treat this disease and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, above and inside the hospital, and then after a long time until that wind is forced out at that place;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the joint;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if you do not see the hair, if the doctor who stops the winds, if it is like pills that rot, and pills of seraphim, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	They are various, according to their appearances and according to the colors of their feathers when they fly.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are those who have great tips, small, hair, and soldered;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those who have II angles, and of those who have tongues, and of those where there are pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which is broken in any member if it is broken according to two manners:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in a principal member it breaks like a skull, liver, heart, pancreas, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it breaks in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, you discover it:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If it is necessary for you to extract this arrow, for death comes after many preparations.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when there is no bad sign showing itself to you, and the arrow is not fully extracted, if it catches, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the skull when the arrow catches and pierces the bone, and the medicine that is on the skull, and the scotomias and fainting and twitching and rash in the eyes, and inflammation and rash on the tongue, and convulsions and confusion of thought, and vomiting of food;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it has come out through the nostrils or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it has come out through speech and sound;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and in jumping from the moisturized wound there is a pulsing that seems like a pulse, and like a flame of fire;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and when this sign shows itself to you, if you hold it back from being extracted, and extract the arrow if it is stuck.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it strikes is that it is near the left breast, and also as if it were stuck in a hard thing rather than in emptiness.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and the arrow may also change course like the birds do, and strike in dark blood, and bring coldness and cold sweat, and faintness.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then sense doubt that death comes.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a sneeze that doesn't involve the nose is that there is no foaming from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's skin changes color, and he sighs loudly and shivers with coldness.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow strikes in the covering of the hip, then break the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and bring great pain and a loud cry.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the limbs move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the sneeze comes from the stomach, perhaps there is something coming out of the wound that isn't digested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow strikes one in the belly, and it goes through the intestine without a stop, there is no hope for the cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow strikes in the bladder, and urine comes out in spurts, causing the patient to urinate, and great pain is felt.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	then know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if it is made of face and neck and throat and shoulder and ajutoire and spine and forcele and cuixe and legs, and the limb that looks like it, are safe according to many arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it does not hurt, so that as I will tell you that it happened to me, do not make it differently.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There was a man at home who had an arrow strike him in the throat and cut through the root of his neck;
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and the other side seared off the grease from the ear, and he was cured without sensation.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And try a string that the chutel fell into the grease of the oil seared off paper, and the string was re-attached, and there could be only the tip toward you from the fist, and the string was great in an arc of Turkish color, all my ears were light without sensation;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The doctors were cured, and no bad accidents happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And try a string from the throat to a Christian, and the string was Arabic to ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved the beards, and tried it as much as I could, and the Christians were cured.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And try a string to him at home, which was his cheek or belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then let it pass XXX days, if he does not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and shaped it, and tested it, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you have an arrow in your butt or chest, and the wound is sewed up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and let the arrow remain within, and do not change its natural dispositions, nor find harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, to whom an arrow struck in his face, and was sewed up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and it remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And I tested an arrow on a prince's son, who had a lump on his neck that was not in the middle, and it was slightly tilted to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat her after she had been lame for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried all sorts of remedies, and could not feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there was no feeling of pain or tingling in her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was due to the arrow's point; I put a plaster of the most efficacious and digestive kind on the spot, lest the swelling increase;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw that it was indeed an arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the plaster every day, and quickly healed the wound, and for a long time after that, the patient felt no pain from the arrow, which was embedded deep in his neck;
et il le me dist.	and it came out.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound, which was opened, and tried it out, and felt that the arrow's point, which had become embedded in the neck, was being drawn out;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	And I adjusted at the opening of the wound by that medical water, until the head of the arrow was visibly visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and I waited well the end for III months, and then it opened so much the wound that I drew out the claws, and picked it up from one side to another, and could not get out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Then I stopped from subtilizing and devising ways to make instruments, until I got it with claws well made, according to what its form will be at the end of this chapter, until I took it up and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctor judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be healed;
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I healed it then, and was sewed up the wound, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or you have not said the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your cure on this which I did not say, for the book cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise masters compare few things well, and on those that are present and deficient, try nine works, and nine instruments, for the dismemberment of strange things that come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not come from limbs or they are fixed except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which is not fixed is by the place where it enters, it is an arrow entering into its flesh, and never remains in place once.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not remain there, let it be left so that the flesh is rotten within, and the course is healed.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is fixed in the bone, and cannot come out, let it remain so for some days, and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it comes out, and if it does not come out, let it be poked inside with a small sharp thing until the flesh inside is enlarged, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow has pierced through to the bone of the skull, and goes into one of the sinuses of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said happen to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If it is not extracted, but left for several days, as the hairs grow even, for if the arrow comes to the sinews, death will come soon.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if an arrow has gone into the bone only, and does not come up to the vitals, and the patient stays without a bad accident for some days, then it is an instrument to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is so deeply lodged that it cannot be extracted, I will administer the remedy as I told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the joint until it is well.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow has been driven into the chest bone so that it cannot be seen, and you seek it with all your strength:
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, handle it with an appropriate instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot extract it by the pressure of the wound, and by the feel of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then cut as much as the wound is great;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and try to extract the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on either side that hold it in place, then remove the core that is lodged in the ear with a pin that you can push, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as much as you can;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you do not break the arrow, but try to extract it more painfully.
