Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out at once, then let the joint between the arrow and the flesh rot; then draw it out, for extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the removal of blood causes the opposite effect, then use what we have said in this chapter's recipe about the cure in its paste;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and take care not to cut the nerve or the vein, and do not push too hard when extracting the arrow, otherwise you may cause harm, or quickly, or firmly, or loudly;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and put the patient in the position they were in when the arrow entered their body, for that is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot do that, then follow the signs the body shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, where it does not pierce anything of him, or the skin is swollen in a place which one can neither see nor feel apart:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Cut away until you can get your hands on the arrow, and then remove it:
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it is now too late:
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, so turn your hand round, until it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then take it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be removed, leave it alone for a while, and then start the extraction again as soon as possible:
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow is stuck in him, push it all the way in:
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if it is stuck, and you have a file, so that the point of the arrow goes into the edge of the tool;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And then push it out again, and if the arrow is caught in him, push the tool out with a point going in, so as to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, so it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is; if you can, then treat the wound as it should be done.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow goes out through the neck or through the belly or through the bladder or through the ribcage, and it is close by, then you can cover over it, if it covers.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and don't cover the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, that is a job.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the cure until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers that are used to remove arrows are similar to an eye, and this is how they should be made:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And in these are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the bit used is also like the beak of a bird, to bite into the tip of the arrow, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the pliers for driving in and drawing out; and thus it should be made.
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the chest common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Veins that are healed are XXXI, where there is a head of XVI, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	II batons which are after the ears, which are called the "dous herbech".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the II arteries which are in II temples appearing;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and II veins that are in II laps of II hairs, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the cut that is at the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the cut that is at the top of the head;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two branches that are at the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two cuts that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are called "augen
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two cuts that are at the tip of the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The five common cuts are V in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	the one is the cerebral, and it is at the left side of the spine, and it is called by the lay people "cut at the top
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "fast" and is composed of the cerebral and the temporal, and it is called by the lay people "cut at the ear";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the temporal is at the right side of the spine, and it is called by the lay people "cut at the belly", and it is above the facial, and this is the one that is spoken of, which opens clearly over the cheek.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the small finger is the sine that is between the index and the ring finger, and if it has II raindrops;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and where the foot are III veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is located on the inside of the left shoe, and the second is at the ankle of the right shoe;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that is called "nesse", which is in the ankle on the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are III veins located those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein that is behind the ears helps with old cataracts and causes headaches;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the vein, as I have said to you, is that you move the head of the patient, and rub the spot where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	and then tie the patient's neck to a pole, as much as the two veins appear behind the ears depending on the head;
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Keep it on your right side, and where you feel the pulse of your right arm, if it is hot to the touch, that is a sign of disease.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lance and pierce it through the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all the way up, cut off the skin and the bone well, and let blood flow as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then extract and bandage it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and that is what I have said about incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The two arteries that are in the two temples, if they are old and hardened, and used to being cold, and to the eyes being wet, and to tears flowing;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the sick person is such as I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	that the patient extrudes his neck until the two veins are exposed;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and put the thumb on top of the two fingers, then sign with the index.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then place the thumb on top of the two fingers, then sign with the index, and insert the lance into the vein at the base, and lift it up, and cut it off, like you did in the other two veins, and cut the blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then clean the wound, and put a finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then let it form, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken about their treatment and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The wound on the forehead heals as well as the headache from an ancient wound in the face, and has migraines and lightheadedness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient holds his neck and twists it until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "casserole", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and hold it up with your hand, or something else, and let the blood come out in the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then cut the neck of the patient, and tie the vein as long as it is healthy and never use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Nevertheless, the flame must not be too hot;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and cut across, for the bone is near, and by chance the flame breaks when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The vein of the two limbs that are in two layers should be used to help with the eyes, and with the plague, and with redness, and with oil in the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their vein is that the patient's neck is pulled out by twisting it with a rope, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	and then the doctor, and the healing of the traveler, a little of long flame a little wide, because there is no fire.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is thin, perhaps it will break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make a fire of the blood, as much as you need, and then put it on wool, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The doctor of the vein of birth if he worths to ague, and suddenly fever, and diseases of the face, as if headache and dizziness come into the face, and even when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the doctor is that the patient strangles his neck, then he holds his birth vein with your left hand, and he puts the thin flame between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well on its own, and the birth will begin to run now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too far with the powder, and make the blood flow according to your need, then let it rest a night, for it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of the fire:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	This is the form of fire:
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the blood is that the patient should extract his hair from one side and another, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and the master standing on one side of the patient's head, and the patient cuts the hair at the back of his head with a sharp knife, then he makes an incision in the blood vessel of the long hair, then he heals the wound with fire quickly, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then he does the same on the other side of the head, then he shaves the hair from the back of the neck with a sharp knife, then he makes an incision in the blood vessel of the long hair, then he heals the wound with fire quickly, or as much as is necessary; then he takes care not to cut the hair of the neck so that the patient does not choke;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	of the medicine of the animals
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	For the medicine of the veins of the lips above helps to heal in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and cuts of the lips, and of the baby and the womb.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the cure is such that the patient sits before you, and his neck is held as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at where they are veined, which one is on the right lip and which one is on the left, and by what you can see that they are black, and by what is between them there are small veins that are black;
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	So make sure the two are correct, and if you don't know them and are in doubt, so make sure the bigger one of the two is on top, and do the same with the veining that is above and below, for this is a good way to do it.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	For the medicine of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The cure for these veined areas is to help after the cure for the cephalic venesection, and it is for the strangulation of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the sun if the patient dies between your hands before the sun, and make him lie down on his back, and look for every corner a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	so save both, and do not cut them too short, for the veins are there.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins that are commonly saved are saved according to two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either cut them at the top with a sharp knife, or cut them finely like a string and are called 'incisions';
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are long and fine according to the width and the stretching of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is sharp and broad, as you see it.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the flat veins that contain large blood and turmoil;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the vein:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtle pointed, and is for saving the veins subtlety, where there is a subtle citrines blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	the save of the base, which is one of these veins, so help the diseases that are there in the throat, and where the neck, and where the chest, and where the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon to bandage him so that he bleeds and burns with the sword which is broken.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and the blood flows, if it comes to stop the bleeding, if it comes as I said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be struck with fire but cut off like a nail.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the base does not open clearly, if it is necessary that you extract it, and change another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you do not want any rain from him, or you heal in his place the vein at the base of the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and it is cut off with fire as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see the place of the wound, it is necessary that you extract the arm, and touch the place as long as you know the pulse:
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	and then mark the neck of the chest, and then tie the arms, and cut off the vein of the flame with a knife;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be careful not to wound in the artery when you see the neck broken, because it is an artery;
eschui la donques.	so avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see coming out on top like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	so hurry up and put your arm on top for a long time, then cut your arm where the blood stops flowing, because it often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	tie the arms, and leave them like that, and do not move the patient;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be afraid, and do not move him until he is healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood does not stop flowing and he comes to you, and if the medicine is not given, then cut the artery, because the head of the shoulder is dislocated:
et estainche li sans.	and restrain the pain.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a branch of fig tree, and cut it, and take one half and bind it well until the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the pain is restrained, it is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, if the cure, as we have said, of powders that restrain pain;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the restraining does not take place in many situations because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm of the patient.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The blood of the wound in the middle should be treated with a paste that is made from the head and the root, as we have said, because it is composed of the bazilica and the cephalica, so that:
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the patient to heat by fire the nerve that is at the root, and if he heats too much in perfection, and he burns the nerve, and he swells and his health is damaged, and perhaps he cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man because of its fineness, it is necessary that you heal it with a sharp instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid opening the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nails, then cut it short.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	the treatment of the head if it helps, that it attracts blood from the head and treats eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to heal by touching at the olive flame or at the marten flame, for it is the most saving of all veins, because it does not damage the nerve nor the artery.

et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and perhaps the way opens in some men the first time, but it does not harm to do it for the first time, but
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	the first thing you must know about healing is that healing should be practiced only to preserve health and prevent future diseases from arising.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the surgeon make his cut in one of the three veins that are there.
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	this is to say, cerebral, facial, and basilar;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and the surgeon should make his cut at the beginning of fasting, and in autumn and winter after dinner when the sign of fullness appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and the surgeon should make his cut on the first day or third day after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The surgeon who is skilled in the art of healing does not need to be instructed in this regard, but he should perform surgery at any time or for any reason;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and does not need to be instructed in this regard, but he should perform surgery on children up to the age of 12 and on women only after four months, up to seven years.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	The patient who is healthy and free from disease does not have a determined age; however, it is appropriate to begin treatment for adults during the hours of day or night, at all times, and it is not appropriate to treat children until they are 12-13 years old, nor women except those who have been pregnant for four months up to seven months. It is also not appropriate to treat the elderly who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone is to be operated on, in whatever way, it is necessary that he urinates in a light enema so that the bowels do not retain the fluid and thus the veins do not draw the fecal matter and harmful residue into the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	not not heal those who are too sunburnt by meat, nor who are yolks, however much they may be, nor droopy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if they are healed after colic fever, vomiting, abdominal pain, frequent childbirth, travail, staying up late, and all that is caused by weapons or the heart;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	and then carefully adjust the humors, if they are thin, with meat, drinks, and medicines, if you have any doubt about it;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and then enter or bathe, if anything does not help them, carefully adjusting the blood, and healing the swelling of the testicles from within the navel to the third joint, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep yourself from work, drinking, lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be lying and resting, and let the healer stand above those who are to be healed, and rub their arms twice or three times, then stretch the tendon slowly, because when it is too stretched or tight, it cannot be bent;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the wound with hands, while the veins swell up and can be felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then wet the wound with a drop of old oil, then put his thumb of his left hand on that vein at the spot where he wants to inject, so that the vein does not get caught in the fire.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that run like strings when injected, and some that are prone to bleeding, so that when you put the flame on them, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus one is vulnerable to this.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, if the wound is too narrow, so that the surgeon must be careful about such things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then begin again a little bit further along that line or on another part of the body if the veins are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if his arm is swollen, and the patient hopes, leave it for a day or two, and do not bandage the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps there will be abscesses.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter or bathe, and then begin again the treatment if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if his fracture is small, or the pain is subtle and you doubt that it will come out as much pain as you see, then take all the fire right to the fracture;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work a little hospital so that his arm is swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	For this often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the arm swollen, do not begin again the treatment, and put on a little oil, for it soothes the body of pain, and is moist in that place where the oil is;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and administer the oil of olive to each vein that you heal, so as to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same mixture makes three times and bowes down when it is placed in its place;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if it is very large, it escapes when it is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there is one large abscess, which often happens, but only when the opening of the vein is small, and you hurry, and place a wet sponge in water and in silk a little warm, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if it remains in its place for a few days without any black or green, then it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see it, put on any thing of aloe or myrrh, juice of calamus, or other things.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times abscesses and appearances occur to the santiment of the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	So then put your hand on it, and if you find that the place is soft under pressure from your hand, then this is the source of the infection.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Avoid putting your hand on anything we have discussed, for fear that you may cause damage to the artery without knowing it.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But let the flesh be dried by the sun until it hardens the place, and then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And according to each person's quantity of virtue, and the color of blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if it is black inside, then let it drain until it is red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	And if you see blood, let it flow until it is thin.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if it is too hot, then let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	For those who are sick and have the need for blood extraction, make the wound larger so that the flames are wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to treat them often and sometimes, and they must be treated by cutting across, not by piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of treatment is saved from the decay of blood and the cutting of nerves, and it is better than long-term treatment with broad cuts.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for those whose bodies require treatment, it is necessary to give them moist water in grape juice.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if it is heated, if three or four times the treatment of blood has been performed; and if it has a cold constitution, if before the treatment moist water in muscatel juice, or honey syrup with aromatic spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and fennel, and well-smelling syrup is given,
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he is ill to the point of blood loss, after the exudation of blood, it is necessary that he swallow beer and aromatic syrup and use other things we have spoken about in the chapter on the treatment of syncope for the purpose of evoking a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he vomits up his food or is ill at other times, as often happens when he is very sick, that he gets better little by little, depending on the amount of his continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he vomits up his food after the first sickness, and he has a strong pulse, then he gets better seven hours after the first sickness, or nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he is sick in another place, he must get well in two days or three.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For it has an effect on the blood in the body that is already heated, causing fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	If it is necessary to extract a large quantity, and to widen the hole as much as possible with a chisel.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and then that you comply with all the conditions for health, and put your hand on your pulse as it heals, so that death does not come from the paine, and this happens many times, when the healing is neglected;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not serve to see that the arm is dislocated and made to move again with pain, and the hole is closed, so you press firmly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is curved, let him extend his arm carefully, because that would be wrong;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but leave it until the second time it heals;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you take the flame to the end of the vein so that it is separated from the hole, and put a little thread wet with water on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess has settled.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if need be, drain the blood a second time, whether it is in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that runs through the arm is connected to the vein at the base of the neck; for it is composed of the same blood.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way of treatment is that the patient dips his hand into hot water until the joints are red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then let him stretch it gently so that the vein shows clearly, then treat it now with the knife, not wide nor long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and be careful not to cut too deeply, and treat it well near the joint of the hand, and if he cannot remove it, dip the hand in hot water and let the blood run in the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is frozen, do not dip the hand in hot water again, for we put it into ice more than into water;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the treatment of this vein is safer from all other veins, as it does not have an artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The treatment for the right hand, which is saved from all diseases of the liver, is as follows:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Extend the arm, and dip it in warm water, as long as the vein is gone, if you see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and bend it across, and cut off all of it, if it doesn't hurt anything;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and don't cut it too deep all at once, for the nerve are very close together and then put the hand back in warm water, if it is frozen in the wound, and cannot take it out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated for as long as necessary, put oil and wax on the vein to hold it tightly together, and do the same for each arm.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The treatment for left-hand savour is good for mouse disease; and do the same as I told you to do for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The treatment for the foot is good for all kinds of disorders of the body, such as diseases of the joints, and also for the feet and legs, old diseases, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of this arm is that the patient dips some foot in warm water, and rubs on the vein as long as it goes away, and then put the joint of the foot.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein if it is at the ankle, and then all along the foot go many ways;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	治 the joint either too large or wide, or at the ankle, so that it does not hurt.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you treat it on the leg, beware of the nerves that are exposed, and treat it with a travers also as when you dig.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot pull them out, put the foot back in water, and let the vein well drain.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is treated for the first time, start again on top of it a second time because its head is salt;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about the nerves, as we have said, and do likewise with the other leg evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The legs of the sciatic vein are at the ankle, and its blood runs to the pain in the thigh when it is time for birth.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of the treatment is that the patient goes in or bathes, and extracts from the ankle eight in twisting, because otherwise the vein does not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then treat it in all ways that you can, and traverse it;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and vale more than you dig because its head is up and it is very swollen at the hands of many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not treat it, so that there is no rain of blood from the foot or back, and towards the small chest, and guard yourself from danger.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and do so much to stop the bleeding that you can see, and then clean the wound, and put cotton on it and hold it in place;
ele est maintenant sanee.	This makes her well.
des sainies de ventouse	The suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Vessels are made of horn, or bronze, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and the suction is done according to two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by hurting and drawing blood, or without hurting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this suction that is without hurting is according to two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is all-over fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and the suction that is made by hurting and drawing blood is made in twelve parts of the body, one of which is all-over the chest;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and II others at the sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction cup from the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction cup from the shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction cup at the ribs;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suction cups extend to the arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the suction cups on the legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the suction cups at the ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the suction treatment does not release blood, unless from small veins that are scattered in the chest, and for this reason it does not fail, as is done with the suction of a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	nor is it necessary that she be bled, nor does fire alone or heat alone help in any disease that comes from overindulgence, until the whole body is deprived.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if for necessity of disease or custom, we treat each hour with the beginning of the month and at its end, and with suction and with compression, then let us do it in turns;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are many who, when they have to breathe, become very heavy.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if it is something that causes them trouble and redness on their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who breathe blood into their mouth, and their tongue has fled, and they are thirsty for blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if it is something that causes them to dream, and see things that are not there, and hear sounds, and taste strange things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and most certainly when it is the middle of the month, we order them to fast after three hours from day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The medicine of the head if it helps with the pain ... which comes from the eyes, and does not come except that blood is evacuated from the whole body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this breathing if it is in the place of the medicine of the head, and does not come except that which has a cold complexion, or which is chatty, for this causes them much harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not necessary for me to tell you not to use them when there is a cold disease.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become dizzy, and for this reason one should put the cup a little lower down due to the doubt of dizziness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation of the neck is in place of the windpipe and larynx, and therefore it causes trouble with the throat, and with the cutting of the voice, and with clearing, and with the swelling.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and therefore it is necessary to put a stop to it, because if it holds too tightly, in this way it hurts or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventilation of the neck hurts like pain in the throat, and it blisters and stings, and chokes, and causes pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in place of the larynx.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And you must order the doctor that he hold his hand in place and not hurt the artery, and that there be no movement of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The windings of the throat are so troublesome to illness of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is in the place of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders cause a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The windings of the arms are as valuable as three veins, because they draw blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the surgeon that he not sew it too tight, for the blood vessels are naked there and can be easily torn;
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The wound on the back is as valuable for the foundation bleeding and for similar diseases as the wound on the leg; it must be large and deep so that it can draw well;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and if it is too thin, it will burst;
et i fai grans plaies.	and make large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The leg wound opens easily because it draws blood from the whole body, and is valuable for the old pains of the kidneys, of the womb, and of the bladder; it also removes the blooms;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are in place of the two feet, and of the two ankles, but they weaken the heart after a long time, and bring about premature death in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner of putting the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and suck quickly, and then place it permanently, and move it evenly, and do not cease to do this, until you see the place red and inflamed, and appear the color of blood;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then dry it off, and remove the suction cups, and take care in the position of the bodies, for there are some who have very soft hearts, and some who have hard spines:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if one is to be injured once only, and one is to make wide wounds, and a little deep;
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the vein is thick, then it is necessary to hurt twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to dilate the path of blood flow
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if it is very thick, then it is necessary to wound for the third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw out blood little by little, then we suffocate just once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want to draw out much blood, then we start again and again;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, then we draw it out completely, and the end is that the pulse is perceived suddenly, and it is necessary to touch a person who has thick and hard skin, and who has been perspiring, so that you moisten the lees of the vials with oil that opens and dissolves:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in a state of estrus, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the period of yew, of mustard oil, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the surplus is thick and cold, take olive oil, or balm, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person with the injury is old and has wide joints, there is no need to put oil on it, but it must be washed after the windification of rosewater, or cold water, or water from mulberries, or water from cucumbers, or porcelain water, or other things like that.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who are affected by moisture, if they rise in such water, or in water from myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have great excesses rise with wine, or with water of wormwood, or with aneth or chamomile decoction, or others.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and they should not be washed by a vacuum before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after vacuuming, and it is necessary that he be warmed up, when he should be vacuumed, and when he has been vacuumed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard those who are being treated for colic, and that their bowels do not move too fast and ignite.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary that he drink cold things, like pomegranates and endive and lettuce at the edge, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and make a juice of pulses, and char on a griddle, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a pale complexion, if they drink syrup of honey and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and make juice of pulses, and make juice of pulses and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and when he vomits, then he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some people once or twice or musk before the ventilation, or after, to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be careful with the water, but it is only necessary that those who are warm drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The vacuum that is applied to the back does not hurt, those that are placed on the liver, and the kidney, and the podagra, and on the belly, and the buttocks, and the rain, and the hunchback, for this member does not feel the pain when it is applied to the skin, and we put it on the breasts when the baby is born;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put vacuums on the belly and the buttocks to weaken the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and bone pain, when there is an operation or a stone, if bone, by its attractive virtue, the operation, or deserts the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and so it is done when you put it on the liver and on the mouse when there is wind trapped, and these suction cups are emptied clean for only so much;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and never are they put together fire, and no times plainness of water is filled, if as the diseases of pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot water, or water in which he has boiled herbs suitable for this;
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup is administered to fire thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it is II fingers wide and half a palm long, and it cost between the middle of the finger and the nail, as for sticking an needle, and be of air, so that it does not bruise the patient when you put it on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and have in the middle a staff of wood or iron to place an axletree, and they are large and small according to the disease and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups of children are other than old ones, and lean that are thin that fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And this suction cup should be placed on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the wax candlestick or the string, and put it in the middle of the suction cup across the staff that is in the middle of the suction cup, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and these two must be on the hole that we have said, so that when you press it, if there is steam, and take off the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the string as before, and restart it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the bellows, then, which is used to treat pleurisy, there should be no water, no pipe nor duct, and it should only be activated when it is completely dry and placed on the limb with great care;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Only in limbs or parts where there are small openings can bellows be applied due to their smallness, such as the lips and gums, and similar parts;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare legs, if they are thin or naked, like two legs, and others that resemble them;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of using it is that when you find bellows that are in clear sweet water without danger, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and dip them into clear sweet water, as long as they remain wet, and do not have anything in their bellows;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then anoint with oil from the wound and from the bellows, then rub the limb until it is red, and put the bellows on;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are clear, and cheer up, if there is a place where one can put a suction cup, one puts it on, for this is worth much after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the level of water in such a way that it covers the joint well, and then pour out the water very well, and then press it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the joint is too sore after raising the level of water, then soak a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the joints are numb;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if there are many joints, then put on vitriol powder, or garlic, and similar things, until they are numb;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the level half of peeled beans, and leave them until they burn at the level, then they will be numb now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more work to do, then take other joints.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the sweats do not want to take, then rub the place of sweat with fresh blood, or you put in an needle as much as the sweat comes out, and then put them on, and sometimes as soon as they feel the sweat, they burn.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are chucking, then powder on a little aloe and sea salt, or ash, they will throw it now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the translation of the provided text:
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The chapters of this treatise are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are beneficial for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know that, dung of the shit, that the wise men have never poured this chapter, that no book or letter has ever read it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the science is strange in our land, for I never found any good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and know nothing, except for the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much and treated the science, and by experience, and by habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly set forth the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore appropriate that we say in this book the sums of words and the chapters where the sagacious mind places his understanding, and remains on truth, so that those who are tested may learn and understand this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture, dislocation or twisting, or dislocation comes to someone, it is necessary that you hurry to save the sick person from one side and the other, if nothing prevents him from doing so, as in cases of weakness of the corset, or paralysis, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or his tension is not very tight, or it is too frequent;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and do not eat too much, that is to say, cold dishes, and char of onions and garlic, and do not drink wine, or eat any greasy foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you are sure of hot chili, nor of expansion of matter in the member;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the disease comes back after initial treatment, it is necessary to resume the treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken nose begins to heal, it is necessary that the sick person be nourished with meat that makes great fattening, or has viscosity, like cooked wheat in water, and rice, and beans, and peas, and dough of wheat, and eggs, and fish fresh, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For as soon as the heat is removed, the breaking must be delayed and postponed.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old and decrepit people cannot be well healed or hardened according to their nature by the loss of limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but if there is no cure, reset the broken bone and join it together with large tendons that hurt and connect the limb, until it heals as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not cut off any of its members, and for this reason it is necessary to feed it with large amounts of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that there are different kinds of fractures in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture at the top is different from the fracture at the foot, or at the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes up and another that goes down, as when the chisel cuts, or as the length of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break at all a small slit.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each has its own tool for restoration, according to what the memory brings back to its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and how the break in the bone is caused by the twist of the lever, and wide apart well by the force of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and if there is no twistedness in them at the base, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can also have twistedness, or a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not move it with your hand but put it on medicine that comes next, and then hold it now slowly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that has happened in the arm, and its two parts are separated, now it is necessary to put them back in an even way, so that the bone grows again.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the bones are healed, let him not work for a day or two, until the bones have healed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it in an even way to the muscle that you can easily and cleanly cut it, and know that the healing of this is lighter than the healing of that which has parts.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	and tighten it, as it should be done.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone has broken into pieces, and its extension is of two parts, whether it be hand or foot, or at the hand, a small member, or two strings, or a string and at the hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and adjust the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are arranged, all additions should be removed from their places that you can, and keep that your work does not cause any harm or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if you think it is not well:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if it is drained properly, and do not pull it too much, and do not press it as those who do so with their work, hot and contracted to the member, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in order, so instruct the patient that he does not move it, neither standing nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and keep well that the member is so secure that it feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when there is no pain at all, or hardly any, and it is convenient to put it in such a position that it does not feel any pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep it so that no twists come when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that the broken members are diverse in size and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs, and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	it is convenient to wrap cloths of soft and subtle linen around them;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those who are fat, such as the leg and thigh:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	it is convenient to wrap with a broad and sturdy linen cloth, for it embraces all the whole member and holds it evenly so that there is no itchiness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	and then it is put in light splints, three or four according to the limb, and held tight with one hand all around the linen cloth, then it goes up over the break and loosens it slightly, so that the break comes away a little;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and make soft the ligature little by little, as you pinch much of the sound part, then take another ligature, and turn very close around the broken place;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the soiled part of the break, and hold it tightly, not too hard or too gently, as we have said in the first ligature above;
