puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the tied threads of linen or drapes, until they are all even, then tie everything above the bandage, and then place your well-made pads on, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something soothing over the abscess, which eases the swelling, and leaves it like that for several days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then hold it under your pads, and be of half a broad strap made of linen, or of oak that you make saws, or of palm leaves, and be according to this form:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the stake which one puts on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and is also far away as it is necessary for the limb, small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold them to the stakes as you did with the first limb, then tie a thread upward, like in the first limb on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	and then narrower upward, however;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and that the thread is light, not too thick nor too thin, and of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, like I have seen in some of the works of the fools who make their ligatures with linen threads that are twisted, and that is a great error, for the ligature cannot be even if it is too thin, and it only comes to less than two inches between each stake.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is stabbed by the nails of the stars after extraction from his natural skin, then put on them a cotton wool or another rag so that he does not scar.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise and the bandage is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not good to extract stars from all the broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, one must not put on stockings before five or seven days, or more according to the direction of the apothecary's knife with care at the same time.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and here is the way of the old plasters in order to restore fracture, dislocation, and twist:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	which you take of the flour which holds to the walls of the mill, and confound it with much egg, and apply this confecting, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plaster which restores the fracture to many dispositions, and most of all to women and small children, for it is not too soft nor too hard.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way of the plaster which restores the fracture and the dislocation and the twist:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take 3 oboles and ladanum and nard and assafetida and gum arabic and mugwort, in 10 zois.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	mirre and aloes, in V Z.
alechil VIIII З.;	 mirre and aloes, and in VIII Z.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and mix it into a powder with milk of ointment.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the complexion of the patient is warm, then use this ointment, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of making ointment that is useful for torsion:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take muggins and viscinin, in X Z.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	 mirre and aloes, in VIII Z.
acaice VI З.;	mixing it with VI Z.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	with bo-arminic X Z., and grind it well, and mix it with milk of ointment or milk of ure, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of making ointment for joints and bones that are out of place and pain:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take another new one, and soak it in milky water and cooked oil, and put it on the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	It is better to use poultices than to apply direct heat; they are good for calming a hot abscess, and properly relieve pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to make plaster that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dry fig leaves and earth leaves of the poplar tree, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of poultice for healing broken bones and reducing the swelling of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take roots of marsh mallows, chamomile, violets, flour of oats, of each a part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind them, and mix them with wine, and heat the member, and apply the mixture of water and coriander juice, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of poultice, stronger than the first, for healing an abscess that has become chronic and is healing slowly.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of marsh mallows, and linseed, yarrow, melilot, and sage, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each a part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind them, and mix them with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken member to restore it except tar made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it must be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on a broken member, to restore it, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way to treat with fire; which is good for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take moldy bread and grind it with water, or feathers, and viscera, and make it into a paste and apply it to the skin.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	Then carefully remove the paste, and pay attention if the patient feels any pain, or if their bones have moved out of place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	If not removed by hand soon.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain arrives at the site, or itchiness, or heat, or swelling, do not delay, remove the paste, and apply the treatment immediately.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And take a light cloth, and a sponge of the sea moistened, and dip it in water, and raise it up to the site, until the itchiness stops, and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, and then put a dry cloth on it, moistened with rosewater or oil, and place a bandage on it, until you are sure there is no heat.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and pain in the bone then begins again with gentle work, and a little turpentine, and do not pull it as hard as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and gently until he is well.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is causing pain and inflammation and swelling, then you must apply poultices and bind it up, if it begins to heal as you have done at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if the limb does not come as we have said, do not dislodge it until after three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never leave it for more than twenty days, according to what you see, until the break heals, and bring the shoulder close to the neck;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then restrain it less than before, and let his meat grow thicker, as I have said above;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see that the head is drying up more than it should, know that dislocation can no longer come;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then arise with warm water every time you dislodge it, and do so for three days in a row, and let the oil sit for a little while;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	By this work, therefore, cut off the members, and cut with great care what is twisted in such a way that it restore the members wrongly.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	This is bad, and if the work is painful, and I see nothing else than to let it lie and do it right.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breaking, and different shapes, and causes are distinct.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For it has fractures that are made by the impact of an arrow, and the collarbone is all broken down to its facet that is dislocated from the bone, like this makes a break or so.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And for this is called "breakage
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	The arrow breaks the bone from above, and it is called in this way "absolute breakage".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And is the wound of these two great fractures or small ones.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impact inside, or a split, or of the jaw of stone, or of falling on stone, or similar.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating break, that approaches the tendon that is outside the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if it is a wound that has entered the bone as finely as our hair, and is a small split, therefore this is called 'capillaire' fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made by a stone, or by a blow, or by a similar thing, and enters a piece of bone downstream, and the break is so fine as to be like the hair that the blacksmith makes when he works on the bellies of his kettles;
si entre li piere dedens.	then it enters between the stones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	and this can happen more easily to those who have a soft skull, like the skull of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and has all these types of fractures that small pieces are broken off like pieces of wood;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by traction on them, and inquiry into the tents, and by the rotten cart that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is caused by what happens when you uncover the bone and rub it upwards, thus creating a black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, take care of potential accidents that might occur with the patient, and if you see no bad accident, as vomiting, loss of understanding, extensiveness, paleness, fever, the eyes getting redder and redder, and other similar signs and symptoms in multiple situations, it is difficult to heal.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a potentially dangerous accident, and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the newborn comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone within fourteen days at most.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the foot, so that you hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue of the bone does not decay, and the accident comes which we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes only to the membrane that covers the skull, so that you split the split part in two;
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and you squeeze the head of the patient by nagging it, and dislodge the bone in all ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more than you can, and the loss of blood comes to uncover the bone, or abscesses hot, help yourself with what is appropriate, and you fill the place with wet linen dipped in oil rosin;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest as long as the abscesses cool down, and be sure of the loss of blood;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then start to open the bone, and it is done according to 2 ways of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one way is that you cut very narrowly at the front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put another in the same way as the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	and the second way is that you have several different size chisels, some narrow and some wide, and some pointed, and made of iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and in oevre lightly, that you do not bleach the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the tooth is loose and hard, it is necessary that you pierce the base, so that you arrange it with care, not completely cutting through the tooth but leaving a margin on top of the point, so that the tip does not go beyond the tooth;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you should have several, so that each comes into its place at the tip of the bone, and you have care for all teeth;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	this is the form of the three ways of pulling out teeth:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing into the bone is that you put the toothpick on the bone and turn it with your fingers as long as you feel that the tooth is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then put the toothpick somewhere else an inch away, and so do all around, then make a small incision into the space of the bone that is between the teeth, and do it more carefully than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw out the bone by your hand, or by any of the tools that you have such as pliers, tweezers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and keep your hands off the brain and the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	and when you have broken the bone and treated it, if it is known that you hold back the marrow which is delayed in the bone from all other instruments resembling an incisors, but it is necessary that it be more gentle and finer than the other incisor;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if he does not delay any small bones, or no scales, if the bone is lightly cut with tools;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then heal the wound with tender and medicinal things that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other way of doing this is that which Galen says, which is more effective;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the loan is very strong, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you discover a part of the bone, where the fracture opens; and so when you have discovered that part, you put on the end of this lens-shaped incision tool, from which comes its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, but the cut is on both sides of the bone so that the cutting is around the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	and then with a small mallet above, so that you gently hit the bone all around, and are well aware of the membrane that is dislocated.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is attached to the bone, so gently hit the bone because the bone is well aware of the harm and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce until the skin, and the bone is cut so little from above, and there are small pieces, then let it be roughened again with a sharp razor, and scrape off the scales with a fine one of which you must have several quantities, to administer in each place the most convenient, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have a very sharp razor, and then a finer one, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair-trimmings and subtle injuries, you must bring about healing according to their repairment;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that has not yet been answered by anyone who has put his study into this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sifus is uncovered, you must take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and dip it in oil, and put it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth double-layered in II or III, dip it in wine and oil and put it on the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and make it with as little pain as possible so that you do not aggravate the disease, then administer on top of another lien, and do not strain it more than it will dry the wound only.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it for a day or two, until the abscesses are relieved, then remove it, and administer medicines as roots of licorice, flour of mustard, powder of incense, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and immediately administer medicines that are deadly without itching;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and guard that the wound is clean, so you do not leave it oozing, nor do you let it assemble bowels, for when the bowels gather on the membrane of the skull, if they are corroded and rotten, they bring great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	For when one applies a mordant substance to the loins, he should not touch it from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take good care, so that no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, if there is doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if black dye comes out only because of the medicine put on it, which has virtue, then you should squeeze a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and one clothful of glue, and put it on the loins.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat in the way that seems fit to you, until he is well.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that the two parts of the neck are never broken from above, for they are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And this bone is cartilage and does not break, unless it is forced or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should pierce your little finger or the palm of your hand at the base of the neck, and make an even cut into it from one side to the other, so that the neck regains its natural shape according to its figure.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, and guard against the patient feeling pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if it is broken in the upper part of the neck, and cannot return to its place, so you put a ray equal to the head of a small stick on top.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	If the fracture is in two parts, then do otherwise, and if you can, hurry to restore the first day;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or ninth, when the abscess is calm, then bandage the head with linen towels, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you patch one with another, if the fracture is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the towels be so thick that they fill the apertures of the nerves.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And say that one should moisten the bandages every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I do not think it is good, but it is necessary that they are moistened in a mixture of egg white and powder of malt;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the bandage on until the bone is hard and the cartilage tough.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never use goose- feathers in place of towels, and if the wound is sore, and hold the break, and blow on the patient;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or fair le cheuil de cuil que tu vois.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come while you are operating, so that you put cotton wet with oil or a drop of aquilone;
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	Or fair le cheuil de cuil que tu vois. And if the abscesses don't come out, then put plaster on it with flour from sesame seeds and incense powder, confited with honey of bee, then put it on thin liniment, and don't tie it tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break in the neck is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it with suitable instruments for this, then cut off the limb, and cure the other wounded animals, and bind them together, as you would do with plasters and ointments suitable for this;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no break in the neck, then treat the injuries and place it in a harness made of rope until it has healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is broken and there is no wound, and the break is not very deep, and it is not broken in two, but only bent inside, so that it looks like a hook, then one should handle it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary that if the break is on the right side, you put your index finger in the mouth of the patient;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is in the left mandible, then with your right index finger, press the fracture lightly and make it equal, and make it equal with your other hand from the side.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the mandible is in two, then you should bring the two parts together, so that they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement of the teeth is, or a rupture, then extract it with a gold, silver, or silk thread, and put on the broken mandible wax, and put on a double cloth;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And put on the cloth a large well-made stake, or a piece of leather that is long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it to the mue (jawbone), and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the figure has changed, then dislodge it on the third day, and then reset what has changed;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and put plaster on, with flour from the mill mixed with egg white or wheat flour, after you have removed the wax;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and place a lighter plaster over it, and if the plaster curates, do not change the patient's disposition until he is well.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the abscesses burst, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, do not put a piece of bone into it;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if it is subtle enough to be cut with ostensible instruments;
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces of bone, and there is no delay at all, if the wound is wide, put on it poultices suitable for that, to promote healing, until it is healthy.
de la forcele	Of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The fracture should be broken several times before, behind the shoulder, and the fracture should be made in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	where it is broken and deranged in two, and there are pieces, and it is easier to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work should be done when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds up the shoulder while the other breaks it;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then make the break even on both sides, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or combing.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you have a need to extend more, then put a round staff under the shoulder of the patient, or a cloth, and make it large according to your need;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and let them stretch out the staff, and hold it with your hand so that you make the break even, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you have the ability to extend further, if you put a round staff under the shoulder of the sick person, or thick cloth or linen, and it is large according to your need; and raise and lower it, and remove the staff from your hand so that you place the break equally, as it should be. If you cannot take off the head of the staff at the end, for fear that it comes apart completely, it is appropriate that the sick person lie down on his back, and put the shoulder under one ear, and press down the ministers on the shoulder downward, until the bone of the staff is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then put the break on both sides, and if you find it loose, then cut it;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and lightly try the pieces, and if the bone cannot join for any reason, then take off the cap from one of the incisions you have made;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you put away this surgical instrument, to save the patient;
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it seems like a spoon, and is not a hair, and also wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the capacity of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and has two heads, so that one is wide and the other narrow, just as it is in the fracture of the bone that you made when you broke the bone;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you secure the abscess with hot poultices if there is little rupture, or if you doubt about securing the abscess with hot poultices, if you cover it with cloth and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, if you dip it in oil with garlic and vinegar, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The extraction of the bone, when there are no wounds and no bruises, is that you put on the bone the talc from the mill and the ash from the oven, and lightly press it with a spoon, and insert a nail into the assembly, if you need one;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	And then take a very long bandage of one palm wide, and then put two sheets on top, and wrap it up.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	And then take a very thin string three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the head of the bandage is hidden.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And then put the string on the break in the skin, and tie the bandage around the neck, and remove the healthy sleeve, and remove the sick sleeve.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And then remove each part, and when you see that the break is holding firmly in place, and you can clearly see that the string is not moving on top of the broken bone, then let it rest for a day, and when you tie it again, if it does not move.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the sick person lie on their side, and put it there when they sleep, so that the shoulder is raised up.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If the break in the shoulder is even with the adjustment of the arm, or you tie the arm to the neck, and there are no bad accidents coming from it, not until XX days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then begin the plastering again, if you see that it is necessary, and holds and leaves it in this way until it is restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in 28 days or less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Then came that the shoulder was broken or out of place, and did not move on either side by touching it;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if the arm is reset according to the shape of the break, and is left according to its natural form, in all ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the powder of the mill with much flour, and light dustings, and put on a double drapery;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then place it on a wide and thin board, slightly larger than the shoulder, and saw the board at the shoulder with a long beard of flax so that the board is cut evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then tighten it with a large and firm bandage so that the board does not move from its place, and inspect it every day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and each time it moves, if it is tightened, and make the board even if it has moved from its place, and lay the patient on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is reset after 20 or 25 days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when the number of days is complete, if it has dislocated again, be sure, for it is not bone that can move lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks out forward and there is no support for it, then turn it over, and the bone, and do as we have said in the breaking of the femur to calm down an abscess with heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the leg
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bones are never broken in the middle, but this does happen a little;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	But it often breaks in the direction of the wind.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it bends towards the inside, and the patient feels great pain, and there is no support, and sometimes he vomits blood, and the skin splits open over the broken bone, and he can feel it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back, and you put a towel between his shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and assemble the ribs with your hands, and adjust it with subtle movement in all ways as you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then put on plasters and bandages thereon the thin bone of salt, or another light stuff, and wrap it in a cloth, and lay it on the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and wrap the bandage around it smoothly at the back, and hold it in place, and unfasten it every hour, and if it relaxes, then fasten it again;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it requires unfastening, for corruption or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, if you hurry, and unfasten it, and remove the plaster, and treat it with ways of cure;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove the plaster, and hold it until it is cured.
de la brisure des costes	Of the rupture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaker of ribs does not come except in large ones after the back and at the head, and do not bend them much because they are brittle.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	And the smell is good to the inquiry as it should be.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoring them is that you make equal the rupture, if it is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put the plaster on, and tie it with a strap, if you need to do so.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the ribs are broken inwards, then the patient feels great pain and a sharp pain, as if crying, because the bone hurts the membrane.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And it bleeds and spits much blood, and that is good for health, and the old have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some of those who serve say that it is necessary to administer meat that swells the belly, in order to push back the rupture by force.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We don't do this either, unless hot abscesses come, if they haven't yet come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If they have come, then let them come.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they said to me that we set vials on the place to draw out the air, and that is apparently right;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, I have doubts that the vials attract the excesses to the place by the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And say that we must cover the place with another dry one in oil, and put tents between the sides to make the area even, then let it be treated with the cure for plague, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone that pokes the cloth, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut over his chest on the side of the bruised rib, and put the instrument so as not to hurt him.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must cut the bone and extract it lightly, and then sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat with poultices until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if an abscess forms, put oil on a cloth and place it on the spot;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal while keeping the joint that needs to be an abscess clean and dry, and keep it clean and dry on the rib where it is, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	No time comes when breaking the bone of the neck, and there was such that he wept;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and to the back of the neck.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it has come to any, and you can see whether it will be healthy or not, if you notice that its hands are soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move them or extend them, and when you prick it with a needle, if it does not feel anything.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many situations; and if he does not feel it when it is held and does not feel anything when it is pulled, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient is cured, if you put the cure on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar things come to the back of the neck, and you can tell whether it is healthy or not, see if the feet are soft, and if the accident that happened was by a sudden wind and excretion without will;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when you have soothed it on his belly, if there is sudden excretion without willpower.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is soothed on his back and he tries to move, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	do not work on its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come from him, then it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the cure is that you put oil on it or butter of sheep's milk on it, as much as it is calmed down;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then put it in a poultice of comfort and drying, and tie it with a string, and tell the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain until he is healthy again.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if some bones are separated, cover them with poultices.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if some bones are broken, then sutures them with thread, and if they are large, with stitches, and treats them with ointment, keeping it clean until they heal;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the head of the collarbone", then take your left hand and hold it level with your right hand, and then apply plaster and bind it on, if you need to do so;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then bandage it, and if there are any separated bones, set them and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	the hip joint fracture
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	For if the bone in the hip is broken, and if so, there would be a little bit of swelling at the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and stretch out long, and lean on the side, and comes to the disease pain in place, and puncture, and swell that breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as long as you are on the broken side;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and knows what is the break and the shape of it;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the break is at the top, so set equal that break, as long as it is in natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inward, so bring the patient up by his stomach, as long as the restoration of that break is made known to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have made it equal, then put on the plaster, and then put a beam of wood or of timber on it, and pull out the break so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and fill the sides with soil, as long as the place is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if the abscess is hot, do not scratch it, as long as the abscess is calm, and then put on that which we have said before;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to restoration, and restrain it as it should, if there is no bad accident;
et c’est li maniere.	This is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The adjutories is that which is between the loin and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one should restore it according to one of the two ways:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	whereone is that you take a strong lever, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And place two shoulders two ties, and raise them up, and cut the patient on one side;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then cast one arm broken on the lever, until it comes to rest, and has in the middle a beam of wood, then cut on one side; and then put one hand below a heavy object or place where it extends downward;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then place the broken arm together with his hands in such a way that the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one should send the sick person to his loins, and tie the hand to his neck, then order two ministers that one should tie who is on the brisurer to his hands, and the others should tie all his limbs, and extend each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then tie the limbs all together, and on the brachium, and extend each minister to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if it is broken near the top of the shoulder, you should put a bandage around the joint, and another one across the back, to fix the break.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and if it is broken on the side, you should put a light bandage on it, without straining, as long as the break is level with the shoulder and with the back.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then make the break even, as it should be, and hold it steady; if a vein bursts, stop the bleeding.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if a vein bursts, if you do not hold it steady for seven days, and put on it an ointment of honey and olive oil, so that the burst vein is calmed down;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then hold it, and the way to hold it is that you put the plaster on the break, then fix the arm with the aid, and place your hand on the shoulder or the back;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and wrap it, and tighten it around the shoulder, and up the arm, so that the arm is in its natural position, where nothing defiles it or where the bone is not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use spices, and put on the break a wider and stronger stake than the others, and leave between each stake two spaces, and let each stake be so big that it passes the break three times from each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then tighten up on the stakes, in this way as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the chaplet on the break, more tightly and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the setting of the stakes and the tightening up, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the stitch, let it be tied for seven days, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	and then observe each for three days that the rash does not grow or come to a head, or that the pus does not come to the member because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the splint, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if such an accident does not come, let it be dislocated only after three days or more, and the patient sleeps on his back, and has his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put cotton into the shoulder joint with care so that it is equal, and observe each hour during the day or night whether the shape of the member does not move, or the ligaments are not relaxed;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if it is treated with the power of medicine, and gives him the food that we have before mentioned, in such a way that the food is at the first layer;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to recover, if it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is fitting that the shoulder and the leg should both be set in place within 40 days from now.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then you must unbind and administer oil and remedies to the injury.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the tightness is bad and blocked, if it takes one or two months to loosen it up.
de la brisure du bras	from the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fosciles," one of which is small and is that which connects to the palm;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and is that which extends towards the little finger;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	in case one of the "fosciles" breaks, either the large or the small, and in case both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small "foscile" is broken, the repair is light, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large one is broken, it is much worse than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small dark spot that is bruised alone, then what is needed is to gently stretch it out and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is only the large "foscile," then it should be extracted with more force;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it on the right side, and darken the pouchet of the hand higher than the others, and the smaller two lower than the others two, and let the patient cross over himself, and I put my cussin in front of him higher than the patient, so that the patient suffers no labor;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the ministers his arms to the part dislocated on his hand, or where he lies, and one other minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then let it be made even according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is in pieces from the break, then let each one be put in its place, and if any of them grasp the other, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do so onto the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the breaker there is a wound, I have spoken about it to the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	so take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration swells come absesses, then I dip them in a paste made of rosin oil and white wax, so that it is not too hard or too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and I dip them over gently, as long as the abscesses are calmed down.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then the bone to char, and I put the plaster of the powder from the mill with a lot of egg, because I put the plaster, and be the plaster of the breaker sooner stronger, and one little more wide than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it must have six plasters or arms in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the breaker is in one of the bones, or in II;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and hold up more on the breaker than on any other part, and always less on the distance, as I said at the beginning of the chapter about the plaster;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and that the drapelets which are on the breaker be soft and moist, and not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and that the thread, of which it is held, be of linen, not too thick nor too fine, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And restore the member and the ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching coming to the limb, it is necessary that you soak the limb with warm water until the itching is relieved;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And let the member do not mie 좁ly rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then recommence the extraction, and if the ligaments are softened and the bone is dislocated, and similar things, then treat it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if it should not come to the member because it is too tight, then you must make it soft a little, and leave it thus for a few days, until the tightening comes again, and then extract it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the illness, then take off the shoulder for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or hang it, then hold his hands to his neck, and let his necks be even, and ward away movement and turning, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this bruiser is healed in XXX days or in XXV, and perhaps in XX days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	are often many breaks in the back of the hand and there comes but little pain.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or wet, so that the patient cuts it crosswise and sits straight before him evenly;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then put his hand on the table extended, and extend the minister the broken bones, and make them even mirrors, as long as they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and put the plaster and the staples, if an abscess does not come, then he puts a stake according to the quantity of the place;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be wrapped in a linen gown.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if it rips at the waistline of the gown, make a patch with some linen fabric, and instruct the patient to tie it around his/her wounded waist.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then take a long linen cloth and wrap it around him/her, as well as the injured hand, and secure it, so that it matches the size of the plant in his/her palm.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it breaks at the end, then you should put a staff on it, and another under the plant, so that the hands are open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and tighten the bond between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if it rips on one of the two arms, wrap it up and make it even, as it should be.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and secure it with the plant, and if you see that it needs a small straight patch to lift the rip, and do not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the rip is on both sides, as in the index or one of the others, make it even and secure it with a healthy hand that comes next.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	And there you tie them all together, so they stay put, or you place them on a stake, like a pouch.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and arrangement of an abscess, and heal those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the chest bruise
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the hip is often broken, and one can clearly see when it turns forward and backward.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is so that you tie them together on top of the fracture, and the other is dislocated.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies face up, then extends each minister his leg to its equal part;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and that is when the fracture is closed with bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the chest, then one of the ties is towards the thumb and the other is towards the heel of the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And if it is near the knee, then let the bindings be loosed from the knee, and let the extension go downward;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then set the bones equal with his two hands, as they were in nature, and then put the plaster, and bind them, so that an abscess does not come;
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is an abscess, let it be calmed then return to your work and to your treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The space is made in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap the break with a hard piece of wood doubled over itself twice or three times, and let the excess go, then turn the leg until the heels come to the root of the ankle, and insert a long pin between the thigh and the leg, freeing the knee from the pin, and bring the head of the pin above;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn on the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then put the wooden splint, and put a wooden Splint on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then place the space between the leg and the thigh of canvas and string to make the strapping even, then begin to tie in the form of three or four twists on the break;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and the more you go up the break, and the less you restrain it;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then take the two legs that you have tied together between the thigh and the crotch, and the three ties that are on top of them, then go back to the dislocation at the head of the thread, as far as you can get it off the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and holds it steady so that it does not move out of place, then leaves it like this, and that he does not come to abscess or inflammation or any other kind of sign;
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it comes, if it comes out of place, and goes back to the one that comes, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that grab hold, if it is appropriate, then you can;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if you cannot, if it is appropriate to split the place and draw out forcefully;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and let him go as we have said, as long as he is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And never break the wrist or elbow as you put on the splint, as in the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	However, when restoring it, do not let the patient move his hand or arm.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the chest is restored in one day, or little more or little less, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the street of the ankle
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	And know that in the street of the ankle there is little injury, but it bleeds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, unless it is just a crack or a gash, and goes to all parts, and feels no pain, and this can be felt well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is done so that what is long is equal to its two sides, as much as it can move without it;
