puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then put on the plaster, and a round splint if you need it, and hold it as we said for all other breaks, such as a hot abscess and others;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	put on each accident what suits him, as long as he is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg break
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, so one is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and comes all like a break as it is in the arm, and for this the restoration is as that of the arm evenly, and the work is all I. And if the two bones are broken together, so turn the leg on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if his subtle nose is broken, then turn back.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	and if the large bone is broken, then one feels great pain and sees it clearly;
et torne desoz.	and turn dislocated.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then bring expansion, and set it evenly, and tie the joints evenly;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	however, if the fracture is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and align it according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two fascines of branches that shade the leg on one side and the other, and are long from the ankle to the top of the leg;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	And envelop in two lees one bendel over and under, and put him in the middle as well, and at this liefness shall not the leg decline to the right nor to the left, and so it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and let no one administer to the long leg, and if necessary, and put the leg so as not to move, and properly made this in the fracture or there is a wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each day the leg, that one may see if there is any abscess or other accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the patient as long as he is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	About the break of the bones of the feet
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	About the ankle, there is no break at all, but from the bones of the feet there comes a break in some cases, and in most situations there comes only a fracture, and it has never been seen to occur on its own.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is an oss of the foot broken, and you see these bones touching each other, put that person on the ground as if he wanted to walk, and then now put your foot on his side, where the bone is raised, and press it until it comes back into its place;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And then put on the plaster and press it down, and put a little table of two legs at the foot of the chest, then fasten it to the ground, and when you have wrapped your drapes and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, then untie the bandage, for you will find the bones even if they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	If there are any of the two broken, if they restore, if as we have said the two with the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then put on the two broken a table according to the length of the two, and make it a little more wide, then put on the foot that I said table, and fasten it to the ground;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three, or more broken, if put on each two a table according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen drapes, and fasten the table to the ground;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and be standing on the top of the table face down the foot of the chest, so that he covers it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things I have said to others about broken bones when we have said it;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and cut off each accident as is fitting.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break of the bone of the knuckle
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the woman's bones are broken, if she is seated enlarged, then she leans to the back part and is held from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the void of nature with cotton illness, and put it as big as I stand;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then lift the woman up, and lower her back slowly and slowly, and then jump the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of nature, and returns the bones with her stand;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, if she pees cotton, and when she has urinated, it is put back, and in this way do seven days or more;
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	then the break will be healed, and if you see it, take a bladder of beer, and tie a cord around the penis, and pour all the bladder into nature;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	Then blow through the tube, as long as the bladder is pushed in.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the break will be healed by nature;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then fill it with cotton, and leave it thus for some days, until he is well.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the arm or of the woman is broken, if he sets it as we have said concerning the bone of the thigh;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and use therein, and listens to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the break signifies many things to him who knows the right way to restore it;
enten le donques.	then listen to it first.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's neck and bottle it up;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap it in strips of cloth, and leave it wrapped for three days or more, and he will be well without hospital.
de brisure avec plaie	of breaking with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For those who have broken a bone with a wound, even if it is a large one, such as the hip or shoulder or arm, let them be healed now, so that the wounds that we have spoken of may testify to their healing.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but the vitriol burns, then, if you have nothing else, continue to restore the break in the same hour, or else the abscesses will come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscesses come out, but continue to leave it until another day, as long as the abscesses are calm and you don't touch them nor on the third day nor on the fourth, for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears on the side that is covered with the wound, it is necessary that you place it at a slight angle with your hand, at a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extensions have not yet been applied to make your hands equal, if you hold this instrument that is made of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and the blade is wide according to the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and because it is necessary for him who uses this instrument to take three or four, according to what is required in each cure of a broken limb;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not press on the limb at your work, and let it be pointed in front, and wide in the middle, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palainche", because it is necessary that the bent head should be placed on the top of the apparently visible bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and he blows once, as long as it remains, and makes them equal one to another.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot take the bone well, you must chop the head of the bone until the instrument has the ability.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, with the handle of an appropriate instrument, or scalpel or chisel, in your power;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	Then take this which is retained in the bone and cut it with a sharp knife and small chisels.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone has been reset, and the patient feels great pain after it, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If you do so that it is in its place, then soak the dressing with black wine vinegar, and properly if it is in the wound;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and put nothing on the wound that has grease or another thing where oil is, for it not to cause infection and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	and then administer the ointment when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, covering all around it, according to the quantity of the wound, and be sure that the wound is not pulled with the break;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times have done this foolish thing, and have brought upon the patient death or corruption;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the breaking be less hard and less sharp than the others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	and if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a good accident will not come, as we have said, and you feel pain at the place, then it is not appropriate to put on splints.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap with strips of cloth instead of hard splints, and bind them firmly.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days to the wound, if an arrow that you have put there has come out, and put on it a healing ointment, as healing tar and similar things;
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be arranged in such a way that the arrow runs down easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day it passes, and he cannot hold it in place, but it comes apart again, because there are little pieces of bone, so that you must take the wound with a towel, and those little pieces of bone that come out cause pain;
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to light, or some other kind of corruption, then you must cure it according to what he said in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	and when the bone is broken and opened on the member, as the shoulder bone or the shoulder blade, and other similar bones of large members, do not pull it out, for many times death comes from it, but let it be until it putrids.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	for fear that he may heal himself after XX days or XXX days, then heal the wound, if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the bruses that come from the sudure
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often come after the health of the breaker, even when it is near the joint, and it is an ugly thing to see the member's figure;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance cannot make the limbs perform their natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care therefore that we are not fresh.
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if he administers medicines that are sticky, such as aloe, incense, myrrh, and sarcollate, acetic acid, and similar things, so that you do not press any of these things, or all together, and blend them with wine that is sticky or with a large amount of egg white or with oil;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put them on the nose in layers, and hold them firmly together, and do not remove them from day to day;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then remove it, and start a new one until the nodules have all been removed;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or hold on a piece of cloth well made;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	because the property of the cloth is that it removes all swelling from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the nodule has become hard like stone, it is necessary to cut it off, leaving behind the crust and removing the excess that appears;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu'elle soit ostee, et la cure tant qu'elle soit sanee.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the member that is weak after the garrison
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	Once the fracture of the bone has healed, and the limbs remain weak and delicate, this may be due to:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	because one is because it was bound too tight, and was not bound as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many ties, and could not bring the member back to its natural position;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or because of a multitude of injuries;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of too great movements, not in its proper time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because it has lost blood in its body, and is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until the blood multiply in it;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and the minister bath, and he made joy and let go.
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then put ointment on the member, so that the ointment attracts all the swelling, and rise it often with water, as much as the swelling goes down to the member;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	two injured limbs after sickness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the form of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural work:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	if one does not believe the foolish people who say that one must break the member all over again, and many foolish men have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these works are to blame, and there come great evils, and perhaps death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	However, if the dislocations and torments are fresh, it is necessary that they be raised with hot water, or with soft herbs boiled, as leaves of walde, and roots, and melilote, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and make the plaster softening, as well done hydronium, and you take the musk of viscose, and confound it with grease of gele or oil of sisa, and make the plaster on;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you take figs, and grind them with hay of hay, and similar medicines that soften the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the arm raised by continuous and prolonged friction with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And make sure there is no movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if his toughness is sore and hardened, too, like stone, then it must be opened with a sharp iron to the bone, lightly incising;
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put resin and study in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is now necessary to bring back sensibly.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if it is delayed, if the loins swell, and by chance it is reset to its place at the loins;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	For so he will not come if it is moved in his urge when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times causes pain and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	first of all, when this happens, if you make the patient well, then leave him, until the abscesses are calm;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the member with hot water and oil, then move it slightly, and heal each member as the wound heals in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chaplets for the dislocations of the shoulder joint up to the edge of the breastbone.
des mandibules	the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	Now let's begin with a sentence about dislocating jawbones, and there are two ways to deal with dislocations of both jaws:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they are a little bones out of place, and softens a little;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely dislocated, and hang down to the chest, and prevent the saliva from leaving the mouth, and wrap the tongue with words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, return it with several different positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and finished, then you must reset it quickly in the hospital, and do not wait.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in this way that the minister holds the head of the patient, and pours a little water from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, there are two ways to deal with it.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands are far apart, to put even.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and command the patient that he softens his jaws, and moves them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let the mirror be made equal, as soon as it revives in its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if they have become stiff, most of all if the two jaws are together, let him warm them with sharp heat and oil, until he makes them slightly flexible again;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not wait to bring them back, as we said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they have been brought back evenly, and the mouth of the sick person is closed well with a softener, let him put it on drapings soaked in a wax made of oil and beeswax, then make it slightly flexible again by moving it;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the sick person sleep on his back, and his cheeks be between two cushions, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor make any effort to improve, but eat soft food, until the pains have ceased, and the jaws have healed;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then cut what needs to be cut lightly, and do not work on opening the mouth for eating or drinking until the jaw is well healed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset within an hour, and are not restored to their places, so that there come fevers and sudden pains used, and by chance stomachache, and by chance vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, know that it is a sign of healing.
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times kills those to whom it was given, in nine days.
de la forcelle	for the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	does not dislocate due to a lack of movement from within the bone and from the top, and does not dislocate at all towards the back, and one can feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the recovery is such that the sick person rises soon after his back and extends his arms.
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the joint with your thumb, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the splint and bandage and holds it in place;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the head that is toward the chest cannot be dislocated;```
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does not pop, and if it does not dislocate at all, if one returns it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put on the splint and bandage and holds it in place, and instruct the patient to rest until he is sound;```
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and likewise is to be brought back the head of the sword when it has come out of its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	I know that the shoulder is dislocated only by three methods:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	that one is when it has come out of its joint in the part of the arm;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part of the shoulder;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and perhaps dislocated at the top, and this happens sometimes;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and do not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and do not dislocate inside for the neck;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and many times dislocated out of its joint towards the sword, except those who have broken their collarbone, because at that time they must be hospitalized;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	except those who have enough collarbone, then let them go, and return home.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	2. And perhaps it happens to some men that there is beating or breaking, and the shoulder becomes hot with an abscess, and they think that it has dislocated.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is therefore necessary that you test it, until you are certain of it;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and so begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And there are differences between them when they fall down the neck, and you will find a manifest difference between the sick and the healthy shoulder, and you will see that there are various degrees of it.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and at the head of the shoulder there is a pit, and put the shoulder down to the ground the head of the shoulder, as though it were one egg;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move at all;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and if it is dislocated upwards, then unless it is hidden, because you will see it clearly on the ground;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this type of dislocation cannot be reset when it is new, or if the patient has fallen ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the way is that the minister raises the hand of the patient upwards, then puts the shoulder down with his hands, and forces the joint back into place upwards;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the ministers leave the hand, and extend it upwards, because it puts it out.
si venra hastanment.	if he will come immediately.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said in days, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and provide soothing and soothing remedies, as a decoction of mint and fenugrec and melilot in water, and be provided;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then let the patient lie on his back, and put on a sock made of equal yarn, not too tight nor too loose, then put the foot of the limb in the sock, and let the minister pull the shoulder blade with ease, and draw the hand of the sick person;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and other ministers hold his head so that he does not move backwards;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	then the shoulder immediately returns, and if it does not return in this way, then you must try again:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and it is that you make be present I home who is greater than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and be two sides of the coast, and bottle s'espaule from the asselle of the patient, and lift the asselle upwards, so that the patient hangs in l';
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and other ministers pull the hand of the patient downward toward the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then with him there is nothing heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And he renames it also in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and is that you file I long stick in the earth, whose head is also as a pistol, and not too thick or too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then be placed on the patient, but that it have drapelets water upon, and the patient be standing on the long of the stick;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then be extended its hand downward from another side forming, and the joint will return to its place smoothly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not return for all these things that we have said, then this remedy fails:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a piece of wood from the two arms of a great and four fingers wide, which has the head ready to enter perfectly into the socket according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then place it on top of the head with a dry cloth so that the patient is not injured, then put it into the socket of the patient:
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and spread your arms on top of the pole, and place the shoulder head on the pole, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on a stick of one span wide, and let the body hang from one side while:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint now returns.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	Then, in whichever way it is, if you put an equal woolen sphere in place of the socket, then put the plaster ready with powder from the mill, with incense and ambergris around the entire shoulder and neck, then remove the socket gradually, and tie the thread to the plaster, and embrace the hand at its collar, and let the hands remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he be placed in a comfortable position so that the limbs are relieved, for he will heal faster;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then after 5 more days or 7, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	if it is stiff and is not softened, then is cured.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has come out of place due to moisture or some other cause, you must apply the cauterization three times, as it is done with the paste of the cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after 7 days, and the joint does not stay in place, and cannot raise your arm forward, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is torn or stretched or weakened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never go back to its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is on the side of the chest, and the shoulders, or behind, it is made by an impact, and the stretching of the arms, and I administer another place;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat as long as it is cured.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after recovery the member comes with a shake and slow move, so often does the patient use it, until that shake is healed, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of dislocation of the head
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	And know that the joint at the neck is dislocated and returns to its place;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it has dislocated from all sides, and most of all in front and behind, and the dislocation is not returned, for we can see it well and feel it well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and repeat according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the injured shoulder with the healthy one, so that you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is chopped, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it in the same way as we have done for the arm, because if an arm comes off completely, it would be a great loss if it were to be reset.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and it cannot be reset completely from all sides, least of all when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	is less painful than other dislocations, and yet causes great pain, and possibly death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is done, as far as it can be reset, so that you can stretch its hand with both your hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and its arms are spread out, and the hands around the neck from behind and from the front, and press the joint to its shoulder blade together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place;
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there is a dislocation in front, so that it returns when it doubles its hand to its place, and tightens the joint at the root of its palm where it has come loose.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not return to its place, then administer a strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and tint them two ministers, so that it does not move to extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm of each part, then you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when you see the joint of his hand, if it is not oiled to soften the joint, then oil the joint completely, until it heals;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, if put on plaster dry with ointment of bee wax, and strain it, and bend the arm at the neck of the sick person, and leave it for a few days, then dislocate it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, then loosen the bandage, and leave it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint does not move well, then begin again with the plaster and the bandage, and leave it in this way for some days, until it is firmly placed;
puis le deslie.	and untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels pain after the joint is reset and still moves, let him bathe and gently rub it, and press until it is relieved.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	Or you put on the joint a fleece of fat lamb, then let it rest for a day and a night, then the bone, and then let it enter or bathe;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when it sweats, gently rubs the joint, then puts on the fleece again, and then bathes;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do this twice or three times until it is well.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see, put on the end of the veil a warm butter, and draw it out;
si revenra a sa disposition.	so that it returns to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The dislocated joint of the hand returns more easily than that of the other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to reset the joint in its place when it is dislocated, so that the bones do not move or come apart, and there is no inflammation or abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And let them put the sick hand on a table, and extend the fingers, and make them even, so that they put their palm on the appearance of the joint, and press it until it revives.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, you must ensure that it is in the right place.
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then put the patient's back hand on a table for extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, put the sick person's back hand on a tray, and make the palm face the joint location.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if the extraction of cold, painful abscesses, and let them stay like this for a while.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	If he cannot bear it, and you are unable to put it back in place after several days, the dislocation will remain.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and do not tell the patient that as long as the hands are wet, they cannot extract anything completely:

Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it well, and there is no fracture, if the wet hot water, and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two bones of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Never are the joints of the hand dislocated from any part, never at the base of the palm or in the belly;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then hold the joint, and push the dislocation into the folds until it comes back, then support the top of the joint, and turn it towards the side where it is joined;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for a day, and then make it even for that day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and do not move it, as we have said, and loosen it from day to day, and make it move, and then reline it with the nut;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do so often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated in the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is well;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do this too, when it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	the dislocation of the shoulder from behind
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, if there is no cure, because it quickly kills the patient.

celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which moves to the back is called "gilbositez".

et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well fastened, the stick as we have said, and the mirrier puts his palms on the back in the form, until he recovers.

des dislocations de la hainche	Here is the translation of the provided text:
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the shoulders only come out due to dislocations, not at all like the other joints;
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	deep and far away, and in front and behind;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and the deeper it is there, and the more it is dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of his dislocations within is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy, it is longer, and the sick knees are more than the healthy, and the sick cannot double his knee on fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and is the place that is inflamed by the abscess, so that the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of those to whom it comes from behind is that this accident is opposite to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of this one who has before it, if it is good his leg according to the accomplishment;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	However, he does not double his knee with pain, and if one makes him walk, he cannot go before, and he holds back his urine, and swells the ankle, and when he walks, he goes on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who is behind, if he cannot spread his knee, nor bend it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is soft, and the hip bone is in place between the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The re-making of this appearance of dislocation is that you reward it if its dislocations are old, and it remains according to its disposition, there is no cure for it;

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	for wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When the wound comes with dislocation, and one attempts to restore it, many times the patient has died:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not knowledgeable in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow to anger, do not be hasty;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at the beginning of things calming bloodletting absces, and let the patient in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, if I now reset the limb in its place, so that the bloodletting absces comes;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limbs are in place, if ministering soothing things to the abscess causes pain, and healing the wound, as it should, of drying ointments;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and with dislocation has fracture, and small bones are broken, if the bone, and do what we have said in simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and keep yourself from going into a state of fear, according to what I have said, for this will cost you your life according to your Creator, and for the sake of protecting yourself and your body.
